Haimen: Yan Zhenji Arrested on Charges 106

Since the collapse of the Decang Money Exchange in Haimen County in 1931, the manager Yan Zhenji has not publicly cleared the accounts. He was sued by shareholder Jiang Wang to the county government. He was summoned repeatedly, but Yan failed to appear. The other day, the county chamber of commerce convened all interested parties to attempt a reconciliation, but Yan was vague and insincere, resulting in no outcome. Yesterday (the 25th), creditors Jinlingchun and others, believing that the delay was hopeless, took Yan to the county public security bureau for transfer to the county government. At the same time, Jiang Wang also petitioned the county government to detain Yan and investigate him according to the law. The situation is extremely tense. The county government is scheduled to open a court hearing this morning (the 26th).

Changzhou: Consecutive Days of Extreme Heat Threatens Drought 107

Since the beginning of summer in Wuyi County, the weather has been severely dry with no rain. The farmland everywhere is parched, the ponds are dry, and the rice seedlings are withering. The farmers are all frowning and worried, longing for rain. However, the heavens refuse to cooperate. During this plum rain season, not only is there no rain, but the scorching sun is raging, and it is extremely hot. On the 25th, the weather in this county was generally 101 degrees Fahrenheit, and up to 106 degrees in factories. On the 26th, it was generally 100 degrees, and around 100 degrees in factories. Today (the 27th), it has reached over 97 degrees by noon, and it may be even hotter in the afternoon. According to old farmers, the year 1856 was the Year of Jiaxu, with double plum rains and a severe drought. This year is also the Year of Jiaxu, with double plum rains. If it does not rain again, a drought and famine will be inevitable, so the prices of wheat, soybeans, and rice have all increased in recent days.

Boatmen Come to Yangzhou Again to Petition

The boatmen and salt workers from the eighteen gangs of Xiang, E, West, and Wan in Shierxu, Yizheng, have been running around and appealing for a living by competing for sail transport for over a year. After repeated consultations between Director Kong and Central Committee Member Wang Bailing, there was a slight solution. It is now heard that Director Miao has submitted a proposal to the authorities to draw lots to buy all the salt transport sailing ships in order to gradually eliminate them. The workers were panicked again and sent representatives Tang Yuefeng and more than ten others to Yangzhou the other day to petition Jin Xin, the manager of the Yangzhou Audit Branch, and to visit Central Committee Member Wang, asking for ways to help.

Nantong: Nantong District Security Conference 109

The Nantong District Security Command convened a security conference at 2 p.m. on the 26th. The attendees included Commissioner and Commander Zheng Yitong, Chief of Staff Peng Longxiang, the county magistrates of each county—Nantong Jin Zonghua, Rugao Zhang Jun, Haimen Zhang Weixie, Qidong Li Baojian, Chongming Wang Bin, Jingjiang Hu Yirong—and the section chief of the commissioner's office, as well as the commander of the Tongtai Haiqi Industrial Special Police Team, Zhang Huan. Zheng Yitong chaired the meeting and reported the significance of convening the meeting. Subsequently, the six county magistrates reported on the general situation of the corps. The matters discussed included: (1) Regarding the merger of the corps and police, how should all the related expenses be collected and paid out? It was decided that each county magistrate should consider the situation in their respective county and submit a written opinion on collection and expenditure to the ministry for verification. (2) Regarding how to rectify the sentry posts, please discuss. It was decided that the sentry soldiers should be local people as a principle, each doing their job during the day and taking turns on sentry duty at night. (3) Regarding how to deal with the surplus and vacancies, please decide. It was decided to determine the number of corps based on the surplus or deficit of the corps' expenses in each county. (4) Regarding how to handle joint defense matters, it was decided that bandits on the borders of each county should be supervised and ordered to be annihilated by the corps, regardless of territorial boundaries. If necessary, the command will convene a joint defense meeting.

Bizarre Lawsuit Between Father-in-Law and Son-in-Law Unresolved 110

Huanbao, the adopted daughter of Chen Changyan in Lvsi, died under unclear circumstances. Her fiancé, Huang Aiqing, sued Chen Changyan in court for bestiality, incest, and theft, claiming that she died after an abortion following pregnancy. There has been no news of her. Jiashan: Kidnapping and Robbery on the Baimao River 112

Xu Xiangqing, a farmer in Baimao River, six li east of Xitang Town, had a relatively comfortable family life. In recent years, due to the rampant banditry, he moved to Xitang for many years. Now, due to the busy farming season, the whole family moved back to farm. After half an hour, they left with the stolen goods, and took Xiangqing's eldest son, Axiang, claiming that a large ransom must be prepared for his redemption.

Hangzhou: Hangzhou-Tunxi Bus Line Offers Joint Transport 113

The Yuxixian section of the Hangzhou-Huizhou Highway (Yulingguan to Shexian, the border between Zhejiang and Anhui) is 61 kilometers long. Chairman Jiang previously ordered the construction departments of Zhejiang and Anhui provinces to rush the construction of each section because the road is related to the transportation between the two provinces. Zhejiang Province built the 31-kilometer section from Yulingguan to Xiakeng on behalf of Anhui. Anhui Province built the 30-kilometer section from Xiakeng to Shexian. The entire project was completed and opened to traffic in November of last year, and the business was operated by Zhejiang Province. Recently, the Anhui Construction Department has mortgaged the Anhui section to the Hangzhou-Huizhou Road Business for the Changtu Automobile Company of She Yu to operate. Ye Zongqi, the inspector and director of the road administration section of the department, was specially sent to Hangzhou to consult with Zhejiang on the recovery of the road and returned the advances in full. It has been officially handed over to the business for operation. The Zhejiang Highway Bureau has also negotiated a joint transport contract with the company. It will only take six hours to reach Tunxi from Hangzhou in the future, which will be especially convenient for passengers.

In order to avoid pedestrians, it drove onto the left sidewalk and hit four people: Zhang Xien, an apprentice at the iron factory who was relaxing in the cool, Zhao Qinglin from Jiangbei, and Zhao Li's young child, Ye Jinshui. Inspector General of Customs Announces National Customs Revenue for 1933 Totaling Over 33 Million Yuan, an 8% Increase Over the Previous Year 115

Xinxin News Agency reports that the Inspector General of Customs of the Ministry of Finance yesterday announced the exact figure for the total national customs revenue for 1933, which was 33,952,449 yuan, an actual increase of 8.3% compared to the total revenue of 31,197,621 yuan in 1932. The detailed figures are as follows: (1) Import tax totaled 26,561,081 yuan. (2) Export tax totaled 23,244,999 yuan. (3) Inland tax and inland surcharges totaled 18,003,322 yuan. (4) Tonnage tax totaled 4,402,648 yuan. (5) Flood relief donation totaled 14,135,788 yuan. (6) Customs surtax totaled 14,126,919 yuan. The total individual income of each customs is as follows: (1) Jianghai Customs collected 17,619,717 yuan. (2) Tianjin Customs collected 4,180,4156 yuan. (3) Jianghan Customs collected 2,041,796 yuan.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Presents to the Ministry of Finance Requesting Chinese Language in Customs 120

Customs Should Use Chinese Language Tax Forms Should Be Primarily in Chinese

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce presented to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating that the Chamber presented a request, and that at the 5th General Meeting of Members on June 17, the Pen and Ink Trade Association proposed petitioning the government to order all customs offices in the country to implement the use of Chinese and abolish the English language as the primary language. The proposal stated that the government had previously proposed that all customs offices uniformly switch to using Chinese and abolish the English language as the primary language. Chinese characters are the primary language used by the general business community in our country, and only a small number also use Western languages. Moreover, customs has a close relationship with merchants, and it is inappropriate to create barriers due to language. As they are both Chinese institutions, they should switch to using Chinese characters to maintain national dignity. The proposal requested to be submitted to the general meeting for discussion and implementation. It was discussed at the general meeting and deemed that although customs offices have used more Chinese for letters and announcements in recent years, or have printed both Chinese and Western languages on the same sheet, tax forms and declarations, which are most relevant to taxation, still mostly use Western languages. This is one of the most difficult points for merchants. It was resolved to petition the Ministry of Finance to instruct all customs offices to use Chinese as the primary language in all documents. It would be fair and convenient to record the case and submit it to your ministry for verification and approval, and to order its implementation. Respectfully presented to the Ministry of Finance.

Letter Requesting the Shanghai Municipal Council to Order All Police Stations to Abolish All Harsh Punishments 122

Chen Binghui and Others of the Shanghai Federation of Trade Unions Yesterday Sent Letters to Various Organizations

Xinxin News Agency reports that Chen Binghui, Zhou Fuzhang, Chen Jiufeng, and others of the Executive Committee of the First Special District Citizens' Federation of this city sent letters to various organizations yesterday, stating, "Dear Sirs, since our country's reform, we have governed the country by law, and all old non-judicial punishments have been abolished. Private torture is strictly prohibited by law. However, the police stations in the Public Concession have secretly set up electric torture, falsely accusing good people of being thieves. Once someone is electrocuted, they confess everything. If they die from electrocution, it is better to confess falsely to avoid death. Therefore, unless electric torture is abolished, the unjustly accused will never be able to clear their names. Previously, patriots Luo Sizhang and Lu Yong personally experienced electric torture and were sentenced for three months. After being released from prison, they appealed to various organizations, but their voices were weak and ineffective. Recently, Cai Yang was falsely accused of theft and repeatedly subjected to electric torture, resulting in serious injuries. Although the court has accepted the investigation, the police station has turned a deaf ear. There are countless others who are afraid to report it. In today's world, civilization is so advanced, how can such brutal punishments still exist? Now, when the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District District Court tried the patriotic martyrs Cao Songshou, Pan Hongsheng, and Tian Shuiyang, the three patriotic martyrs all said that they had suffered severe torture in the police station and could not bear the pain, so they had to obey the police station's instructions. Right and wrong were not determined by their own will. Hearing their words and considering the past facts, there must be countless people who have been unjustly accused under electric torture in the police station. Such inhumane and illegal actions are extremely hateful. Therefore, we propose that your association send a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council as soon as possible to order all police stations to abolish electric torture and other private punishments in order to respect human rights. This would be a great deed."

Fourth Marine Personnel Examination Held in Wusong Yesterday 125

Ministry of Transportation Dispatches Gao Tingzi to Shanghai to Supervise Examination The Three-Day Examination Began Yesterday with 140 Candidates

The fourth marine personnel examination of the Ministry of Communications began yesterday at Wusong Merchant Marine School. The examination period is three days, divided into marine engineering and navigation. For the sake of caution, the Ministry of Communications specially dispatched Gao Tingzi, director of the Maritime Administration Department, Chen Shaoji, chief of the Maritime Administration Section, Wu Yinghui, naval staff member Liao Jingfang, and Xu Zufan, president of the Merchant Marine School, to form an examination committee, and Gao Tingzi was appointed as the chief examiner. All officials arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning and went to the school to preside over the examination. It is estimated that more than 300 Chinese and foreign marine personnel registered for the examination, which is more enthusiastic than in previous sessions. Among them, some could not be present due to job commitments, so only 143 people participated in the examination. Among them, there were two German marine personnel, seven Japanese, two Norwegians, and two Portuguese. The rest were Chinese. Seventy-one took the marine engineering examination, and seventy-two took the navigation examination. It was rumored yesterday that the Japanese consulate requested a change in the examination system. A Guowen reporter specifically asked Director Gao about the truth of the matter. According to him, the Japanese marine personnel could not understand Chinese or English and were afraid that it would be difficult to take the examination, so they temporarily asked someone to translate. There were no problems, and the Japanese marine personnel took the examination as usual. As for changing the examination system, he had not heard of it beforehand and had not received any orders from the Ministry of Communications. The purpose of the examination is to ensure maritime safety and to protect the lives of marine personnel. It does not disregard their skills because they are not educated. This has been implemented in European and Western countries for a long time. There are many benefits and no disadvantages for the marine personnel taking the examination, so participation is voluntary. After a ship is set off, the lives and property of the entire ship are entirely in the hands of the three or five marine personnel. After the examination, not only is the shipping company relieved, but the marine personnel themselves have more protection in their services. More than 150 people who registered but did not take the examination will be given another opportunity to take a supplementary examination. As for the fifth examination, it has not yet been scheduled. The examination schedule and subjects are as follows: Day 1: Chinese, foreign language, cargo handling, ship management, marine personnel duties. Day 2: Navigation, marine engineering, shipbuilding, marine engineering knowledge, piloting, compass science, meteorology. Day 3: Scientific management, chart application, navigation instruments, seamanship, maritime laws and regulations, collision avoidance regulations, signals, swimming, etc.

National Railways: New Train Timetable Ready; Direct Shanghai-Tongguan Freight Train Service Begins Simultaneously; Songhu and Caoyong Sections Remain Unchanged 127

In accordance with the resolutions of the National Railway Joint Timetable Conference, all railways have revised their train timetables, which are scheduled to be implemented on the 1st of next month. Direct freight train service between Shanghai and Tongguan, as well as through train service to Zhenjiang and Jiaxing, will also begin simultaneously. Details are as follows:

Preparations Completed on All Routes 128

All national railways will use the timetable of the 301st and 302nd Shanghai-Beiping through trains as the standard for all military train schedules, ensuring seamless connections. All routes, including Jinghu (Beijing-Shanghai), Huhangyong (Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo), Jinpu (Tianjin-Pukou), Beining (Beijing-Shenyang), Longhai, Jiaoji (Jiaozhou-Jinan), Pingsui (Beijing-Suiyuan), Pinghan (Beijing-Hankou), Zhengtai (Zhengding-Taiyuan), Daoqing (Daokou-Qinghua), Xiang'e (Hunan-Hubei), Zhuping (Zhuzhou-Pingxiang), and Zhegan (Zhejiang-Jiangxi), have finalized and printed their timetables. All preparations are complete and will be implemented as scheduled. The standard timetable for the Shanghai-Beiping through trains is recorded as follows: The 301st train departs Beiping at 15:05, departs Tianjin East Station at 18:20, departs Nanjing at 24:00, and arrives at Shanghai North Station at 7:40. The 302nd train departs Shanghai North Station at 16:00, departs Nanjing at 22:55, departs Tianjin East Station at 7:30, and arrives at Beiping at 10:24. Fares remain the same.

Direct Shanghai-Tongguan Freight Train 129

The Beijing-Shanghai, Tianjin-Pukou, and Longhai Railway Bureaus have been ordered by the Ministry of Railways to operate the Shanghai-Tongguan freight train. The train will originate in Shanghai, attach to the Shanghai-Beiping freight train to Xuzhou, and then transfer to the Longhai Railway freight train to Tongguan. The Tongguan-originating train will attach to the Longhai Railway freight train, arrive in Xuzhou, and then attach to the Pinghu (Beiping-Shanghai) freight train to Shanghai. It is now scheduled to begin direct freight train service on July 1st, designating the 403rd Tongguan-Shanghai joint freight train and the 404th Shanghai-Tongguan joint freight train for operation. If the freight cars do not fill an entire train, they may still attach to the Shanghai-Beiping freight train.

Caoyong and Songhu Sections Remain Unchanged 130

The train schedules of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways, except for the Caoyong (Cao'e River-Ningbo) and Songhu (Shanghai-Wusong) sections which remain unchanged (i.e., the April 1st plan), will be revised for the Beijing-Shanghai, Shanghai-Hangzhou, and Gongzha sections. Starting next month on the 1st, a special Zhenjiang-Jiaxing mixed passenger train will operate daily, departing once each day from Zhenjiang Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and Jiaxing Station on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway.

Chaozhou Merchants: Petition Against Reducing Import Tax on Foreign Sugar; Telegram to the Central Government 131

The Chaozhou Guild, upon receiving news that the Ministry of Finance planned to announce new import tariff regulations with a reduction in the tax rate on foreign sugar, immediately sent a telegram on behalf of the sugar industry to the Nanjing National Government's Ministry of Finance and Ministry of Industry, stating: "To the esteemed Ministries of Finance and Industry of the Nanjing National Government: We have received a telegram from the Shantou Local Sugar Industry Association, stating that the Ministry of Finance is scheduled to announce new import tariff regulations on July 1st, which include a reduction in the tax rate on foreign sugar. Merchants have been deeply alarmed by this news, and the local sugar industry will be greatly affected. It is our understanding that the rural areas of Chaozhou and Meizhou rely on local sugar production to sustain their economy. Since the dumping of imported foreign sugar, the local sugar industry has suffered a blow and has been in decline, leading to the collapse of rural areas. Fortunately, our Ministry of Finance increased the import tax rate on foreign sugar the year before last, giving the local sugar industry a chance to gradually recover. If the tax rate on foreign sugar is lowered again, providing another opportunity for imported dumping and furthering their conspiracy of aggression, the national product source will be deprived, and the people's livelihood and economy will suffer even more. The esteemed guild shares a common origin and fate, and we request that you quickly telegraph the government to ensure that the original tax rate for imported foreign sugar is maintained when revising the new import tariff regulations, and that it not be reduced again, in order to protect domestic products and benefit the people's livelihood, etc.' Upon receiving this, we believe that lowering the import tax rate on foreign sugar would open the door for foreign sugar to dump its products. Although this is currently based on rumors and has not been confirmed, we cannot remain silent about what we perceive as a danger. We hereby telegraph this to your ministries for verification and request that you approve the collection of import tax on foreign sugar according to the original plan, in order to align with the commercial situation. We would be grateful for your convenience. Shanghai Chaozhou Guild, respectfully."

Number of Silk Factories in This City Increasing Daily; Overseas Silk Sales Still Sluggish; Prices Remain Unchanged; Future Still Difficult to Be Optimistic 138

Due to the impact of Japanese silk dumping in Europe and America last year, the silk factories in this city suffered a sharp drop in prices and were unable to maintain operations, leading to successive closures. After the spring cocoons came on the market this year, the factories have gradually resumed operations, reaching over 30 factories. However, silk prices remain unchanged, and the future is still difficult to be optimistic about. The following is a report by a Dagongbao reporter on the situation:

After the spring cocoons came on the market this year, the cocoon quality was excellent, better than in previous years. Therefore, silk merchants are actively trying to reopen factories. In this city, there are a total of 113 single and double empty silk factories. Those that have reluctantly reopened in mid-March and April include: Hengcang in Miaotou, Zhabei District; Yingfeng in Tanjiaqiao; Fengtai in Dayangqiao; Gongda and Huasheng on Zhongxing Road; Fuchang in Pengpuqiao; Xinglun and Yufeng in Gujiawan; Jiyu and Meifeng on Gonghe Road; Yutai in Tanziwan; Desheng on Liuying Road; Yongting in Yanjia Ge; Yuanxing and Yuanji on Yutong Road; Yutong and Yifeng on Meiyuan Road; Xiangmao on Tiantong Road; and Baotai Factory No. 1 in Dapuqiao, Nanshi District; Yuanyou on Alabaster Road in the Concession, etc., totaling 215 factories. Recently, five more factories have announced their reopening starting today: Jingwei in the Concession; Qianyuan on Changan Road, Zhabei District; Fusheng in Gujiawan; and Maofeng and Tongchang on Yutong Road. In total, 30 factories in the city have reopened successively, and about ten more factories are expected to resume operations in early June.

According to people in the silk industry, the spring cocoon season in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has ended. The summer silkworms in Linping, Pinghu, Fengde, Jiaxing in Zhejiang, and Wuxi and Zhenjiang in Jiangsu are hatching smoothly and developing well. The early batches of three-sleep silkworms are still feeding on leaves, and the late batches have also started feeding. If the weather does not change, a bumper harvest is expected.

The European and American silk markets, such as New York and Lyon, have been sluggish recently due to the hot weather. Silk weaving factories are planning to take holidays early, and current silk stocks are high. Most have stopped purchasing, so Chinese silk sales remain sluggish, and prices remain unchanged. Recently, the opening price for high-quality Shanghai factory silk is about 540 yuan per dan, and yellow coarse silk is about 330 yuan per dan. According to the cost calculations of the silk factories in this city, each dan still suffers a loss, so the future of the silk industry is difficult to be optimistic about.

Sino-Foreign Relief Association: Acceptance of Stone Works on the Eastern Embankment of Gaoyou 142

The Sino-Foreign Relief Association on Renji Road was responsible for the project of converting the breach on the eastern embankment of Gaoyou into stone works. After the project was completed, the Jiangsu Provincial Government was requested to send personnel to inspect and accept it. The original letter from the Provincial Government to the Association and the report on the inspection and acceptance process are recorded below:

Provincial Government Official Letter: "According to the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau, the project to convert the missing parts of the embankments at Tangjunlou, Miaoxiangkou, and Qigongdian on the Eastern Embankment of Gaoyou into stone construction has been inspected and found to be solid, well-constructed, and in accordance with the specifications. The Association, despite the difficult economic situation and the difficulty in raising funds, did not avoid difficulties and completed this important project. The project leaders carried out the bank protection work and strived for solidity. Since the start of construction, progress has been rapid. Before the flood season, this major project was completed, demonstrating effective leadership and dedication to public service. The aforementioned has been submitted. After review, this bank protection project is crucial for flood prevention and is extremely important for the livelihoods of the people of northern Jiangsu. However, the project is difficult and costly, and the province is facing the aftermath of disasters and is unable to bear it alone. We deeply rely on the Association's commitment to helping those in need and raising funds from various sources to achieve this great undertaking and create great benefits. The gratitude is not limited to the people of the lower reaches of the river. In addition to instructing that it be placed on file, a copy of the original document is attached for your reference. This letter is addressed to the Sino-Foreign Relief Association."

Furthermore, a report from Xu Dingkang, Director of the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau, to the Provincial Government states: "I, the undersigned, have previously received instructions from your office stating that 'We have approved a public letter from the Sino-Foreign Relief Association stating that our association previously received a letter from your government discussing the repair of the missing parts of Tangjunlou, Miaoxiangkou, Qigongdian, and other places on the Eastern Embankment of Gaoyou and converting them into stone construction. Our association agreed to undertake this project as it concerns disaster prevention and good deeds. We have publicly appointed Mr. Huang Qinglan as the director and Mr. Wang Baohuai as the deputy director of the project. After setting up an office to prepare for construction, we sent a letter to your government through the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau to place it on file. We have now received a letter from the Gaoyou office stating that the stone construction project for the three missing parts of Tang, Miao, and Qi has been completed according to the estimated styles and specifications. We should send personnel to inspect and accept them as soon as possible so that each work surpasses the standard and can be opened at an early date to complete the procedures. We correspondly request that your government instruct the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau to jointly inspect them and order the local flood control personnel to strengthen the defense. I respectfully request that this be investigated and implemented promptly,' etc. After receiving this instruction, we ordered the Gaobao Section Engineering Office to order the flood control personnel to properly safeguard it and sent Secretary Shen Baozhen and Technical Officer Sun Choupei to jointly inspect it. Afterwards, according to the report from the secretary and technical officer, we arrived in Gaoyou and found that Tangjunlou, Miaoxiangkou, and Qigongdian had old brick and stone bank protection before the levee was breached on the canal. The levee was restored in the 21st year of the Republic of China, but due to time constraints, it was temporarily replaced with brushwood work. However, the situation was steep, and the flow was too strong. Now, the engineering to build a block stone slope bank protection has a slope foot that is still at the original site of the brushwood work. The slope decreases, occupying the main levee. The west slope is still in the east slope, helping to build it back into place. The levee surface is three zhang. The entire stone construction foundation is signed with three rows of wooden piles, with each pile two chi apart and each row one chi and five cun apart, forming a plum blossom shape. The slope surface is made of a 1:3:6 ratio of reinforced concrete cover, and the slope foot has a reinforced concrete bottom sill with the same proportions as the cover. In the middle, there is a reinforced concrete longitudinal reinforcement with the same proportions as the top and bottom, and every four zhang, there is a longitudinal rib forming a grid shape. Each grid in the middle is leveled with block stones, and the gaps are all filled with a 1:3:6 ratio of cement slurry, and the slope surface seams are also uniformly inlaid with stone construction. Both ends of the slope are built with wrapping heads. The lower sill is rounded and connects to the soil slope, and a reinforced concrete longitudinal rib is made on the outer end of the wrapping head, penetrating into the levee body to prevent water flow erosion. The Tang and Miao projects have 13 temperature expansion joints. Before construction, a dike and soil enclosure was built outside the levee foot to prevent water from rising and hindering the progress of the project. The entire project has a plan diagram that can be used for verification. The undersigned has now inspected and accepted them one by one according to the original plan. All earth and stone work measurements are more than the original estimate, and the materials are solid and the work is strong and the workmanship is proper. Before receiving the order, the undersigned respectfully reports the on-site inspection and acceptance situation and attaches two sheets of acceptance form for your review and transfer. This is a matter of virtue and convenience, etc. Enclosed is a piece of the acceptance sheet. It was found that Tang, Miao, and Qi in the eastern levee of the canal are located in Lincheng, a place of strategic importance. They were all levee breaches in the 20th year of the Republic of China. When handling the post-disaster project, the Sino-Foreign Relief Association allocated a large sum of money to undertake the main project of closing the gaps, and the association also built brushwood work on the three places near the river to provide protection. The association's spirit of public service and righteousness is commendable. After the project was completed, the bureau was deeply concerned that the new dike was not strong and the brushwood was easily decayed, making it difficult to guarantee its permanence. There was a plan to convert the brushwood into block stone to protect the bank, but due to the lack of financial resources, it was not easy to implement. The association once again generously allocated money to undertake the project. It is thought that the association is working on the project at a time when financial resources are exhausted and it is not easy to raise funds from all parties. It does not avoid difficulties and is able to complete this important project in order to achieve a permanent solution.

It shows deep concern for river defense. We are deeply grateful. As for the personnel in charge of the project, in addition to carrying out the bank protection project, they also strive to ensure that the work is solid and the materials are strong. They also consider the importance of canal traffic and do not hesitate to increase construction costs to rebuild the river enclosure so that the progress of the project and navigation traffic do not interfere with each other.

They also add an extra layer of bracing and broaden the embankment body to make it firmer. The planning is thorough and admirable. Since the start of construction, progress has been rapid. Each levee project was completed in the shortest period of time before the floodwaters rose. The project was carried out by the person in charge in an organized manner with diligence and a sense of public duty.

The actual situation of the Gaoyou eastern embankment stonework inspection conforms with the situation described above. I hereby write to report to Jiangsu Provincial Government Chairman Chen.

Rickshaw Pullers Support Committee's Plan 143

The Public Concession Municipal Council's information office released a message, stating that recently, the rickshaw pullers in the Public Concession have been increasingly supportive of the Municipal Council Management Committee's reform plan. Representatives of rickshaw pullers visit the committee every day to talk. On the 25th of this month, 643 rickshaw pullers jointly submitted a petition, which stated in part: "Recently, rickshaw owners have been actively using the magic of money to buy off a tailor and a street stall vendor, pretending to be rickshaw puller representatives, in an attempt to oppose the various plans and implementation of your bureau. We implore you to severely punish them so that the various plans and implementation of your bureau can proceed. The hundreds of thousands of hardworking rickshaw pullers in the city, no matter what happens, vow to support the various plans and implementation of your bureau and vow to work together as a support. We implore your bureau to approve the implementation. For the purpose of reducing rickshaw rents, please limit the fee to ten jiao per day, plus one jiao for the rickshaw puller relief fund, starting from August 1st of this year. We also request that the rickshaw rent be set at eight jiao per day starting from January 1, 1935, in order to relieve the poor and save the masses from being perpetually oppressed by high rents and to prevent rickshaw owners from monopolizing and deceiving. Helping tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers is a public service that benefits both sides."

The committee also received a petition from a genuine rickshaw owner, requesting that the Municipal Council issue licenses directly in the future because currently, they are issued through a proxy donor who charges the rickshaw owner a fee of up to 15 yuan and 67 cents per license each month. The petition also stated that many rickshaw owners are suffering from this hardship and being exploited by the proxy donor, who does not own any vehicles himself. These rickshaw owners greatly desire the Municipal Council to issue rickshaw owner certificates so that the rickshaw owners can collect the licenses themselves. However, these proxy donors are currently trying their best to prevent rickshaw owners from coming to the bureau to collect the certificates in order to protect their illegal profits.

Although the proxy donors have such intentions, it is said that many rickshaw owners have come to the Municipal Council to petition and obtain certificates in recent days. As for the rickshaw owners who are hesitating and not collecting certificates, they may regret their miscalculation when the new licenses are issued in August.

Polish Man Forges Passport: Trial Concluded Yesterday, Awaiting Sentencing 149

Polish nationals, Stanisieyski (transliteration) and Pour Horski (transliteration), were arrested by the French police last month in connection with the case of a large amount of jewelry stolen from the Siberia Jewelry Company at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Jiangxi Road in the Public Concession last year. Although they were found to have no suspicion of theft after interrogation, it was discovered that the Polish passport presented by Stanisieyski was forged, constituting the crime of forging official documents under Articles 229 and 133 of the Criminal Code. They were transferred to the Second Special District Local Court and ordered to await further verification on a later date. Yesterday morning, Judge Qiu Huan Ying continued the trial in the Criminal Court No. 8. During the interrogation, Stanisieyski stated that Pour Horski had lent the passport to a civilian, who had replaced it with his own photo and used it to go to Harbin and other places. He claimed he was unaware that it was forged. When questioned, Pour Horski stated that the civilian had bought the passport from a Jew in Tianjin for 25 yuan last August, and the civilian had taken it to Hong Kong, Guangdong, Fujian, and other places before lending it to Stanisieyski for his use. The Polish Minister to China, Weideng Te'er (transliteration), appointed lawyer Chen Ying to the court to represent and state everything. Judge Qiu verified the statements, announced the conclusion of the trial, and scheduled a sentencing date. The two defendants were returned to custody to await further instructions.

Page 14

Without Rain in the Rainy Season, Drought is Imminent: Rice Prices Soar to Over Ten Yuan 158

According to Shenshi News Agency, since the seedlings were planted this spring in the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, except for the area north of the Yangtze River, farmers have been in great need of rain. However, the weather has been dry and lacking in rain. Therefore, farmers in the countryside have been busy drawing water. At present, the streams and rivers in various counties have been completely dry and depleted, and people are panicked. Since clouds and rain have not arrived, the strange phenomenon of praying to gods for rain has emerged again. However, despite sincere efforts, the sun is still blazing and the flames are scorching. There is not a single cloud in the sky to comfort the yearning. As a result, food prices have risen uniformly. The prospects are particularly worrying. A Shenshi News Agency reporter learned the following from the Grain Trade Association yesterday:

Rice Market is Firm 159

The prices of both local and guest rice in this city are trending upward. Within a week, each dan has risen by about one yuan or more. Currently, the highest price for local rice is ten yuan and one jiao, and the lowest is eight yuan and one jiao. Among the guest rice, Jiangxi late-season machine rice is eight yuan and five jiao, Hunan rice is seven yuan and nine jiao, Wuhu rice is seven yuan and seven jiao, Hankou rice is six yuan and six jiao, and Shashi rice is six yuan and two jiao. In the past two days, the Fujian and Beiyang gangs have made large-scale purchases, and the market has become more active. If there is still no heavy rain during this yellow plum season, the drought will inevitably be more severe, and the price of rice will inevitably continue to rise. Shanghai citizens who have been eating cheap food in recent years are afraid that they will suffer the same hardship as farmers. Since the customs authorities have levied import duties on foreign rice, it has disappeared from the market and there is no market price. The 200,000 bags of foreign rice purchased by foreign merchants last year were later sold to rice shops in Doumi Street at a low price because no one was interested in them. Now, they are gradually becoming active, with an asking price of seven yuan and seven jiao. There is hope that the price will rise to eight yuan soon. However, importing foreign rice is still not possible under the current circumstances. With a rice tax of about three yuan per dan, plus shipping costs, the cost is too high and it is still difficult to sell.

Gu Xin Yi's Comments 160

According to Mr. Gu Xinyi, a leader in the grain industry, who expressed his views to a Shenshi News Agency reporter, the drought in various provinces today will inevitably affect the rural economy as farmers' autumn harvests decrease. He hopes that the government can use large sums of money to purchase and store large quantities of rice, wheat, flour, and other grains before the grain prices rise to the highest limit and distribute them to major cities in various provinces. When farmers lack food, they can be lent and sold at a fair price to alleviate their shortage, so that farmers will not be completely bankrupt due to the drought. This will be of great benefit to the rural revitalization work. He hopes that the government will take action quickly.

A Good Place to Cool Off: Take a Pleasure Trip on the River │ Municipal Ferry Opens Evening Cool-Off Service │ Wusong · · · · · · From July 1st, Minhang · · · · · · From July 7th 161

The Municipal Ferry Administration Office of the Shanghai Industrial Trust and Savings Society, due to the recent hot weather, which has broken the 60-year temperature record, and the lack of places to cool off in Shanghai, where it is miserable to be in a stuffy room at night, is opening the Wusong evening cool-off service early. It is scheduled to start on July 1st. This year, the Minhang evening cool-off service has also been added and will start on July 7th. The details are recorded below:

Equipment on the Ship 162

The ship used for this evening cool-off service is the most perfect and magnificent No. 5 ferry of the office. There are comfortable and clean white canvas chairs on the deck. Fresh flowers are arranged next to the seats, with a fragrant aroma. The ship is also equipped with a wireless radio to receive famous Chinese and Western music from various places. The railings are fully decorated with red and green electric torches. The air in the Huangpu River is clean and especially cool in the evening. Gentlemen and ladies from all walks of life, if you want to find a good place to cool off, this is definitely it. In addition, the ship also has exquisite Western pastries and refreshing drinks for customers to order at any time.

Wusong Night Service 163

Starting from July 1st, it will run every night. The times are as follows: "Downstream" Shanghai departs at 8:30 p.m., Donggou departs at 9:10 p.m., Gaoqiao departs at 9:40 p.m., Wusong arrives at 10:15 p.m.; "Upstream" Wusong departs at 10:30 p.m., Gaoqiao departs at 11:30 p.m., Donggou departs at 11:50 p.m., Shanghai arrives at 12:30 a.m. The fares are: "Special Class" one-way 8 jiao, round-trip 1 yuan and 6 jiao; "First Class" one-way 4 jiao, round-trip 8 jiao.

Minhang Night Service 164

The office believes that Minhang is located on the Huangpu River, with beautiful scenery and elegant public and private gardens, so starting this year, the Minhang night service has been added to benefit travelers. It will run every Saturday and Sunday starting from July 7th. It runs directly from Shanghai to Minhang without stopping along the way. The time is 8:30 p.m. departure and 12:30 a.m. return to Shanghai. The "Fares" are "Special Class" one-way 8 jiao, round-trip 1 yuan and 6 jiao, "First Class" one-way 4 jiao, round-trip 8 jiao.

Private Car Hire 165

Since travelers returning to Shanghai are already at 12:30 a.m., it is not easy to hire a car. The office has specially agreed with Xiang Sheng Motor Company to wait at the pier. Regardless of the distance, the fare is one yuan, which is especially convenient. The ship tickets are sold at the bronze statue pier on the Bund in Nanjing Road. For other contact matters, please write to the Municipal Ferry Management Office of the Shanghai Industrial Trust and Savings Society at No. 66 Tianjin Road.

Engagement on the River 166

Mr. Shen Shu Kui, the former county magistrate of Nanhui County, son Baoqi, is scheduled to be engaged to Ms. Yuan Huifen on June 30th. In view of the hot weather and the lack of cool places on land, a special ship was chartered from the Municipal Ferry Administration Office to hold the engagement on the ship. It is scheduled to depart at 5:30 p.m. and go straight to Wusong, returning in three hours. An engagement on the river is also a good story. It is heard that the office has an original method for chartering ships, and the price is not too expensive.

Xu Shiying Announces: Preliminary Construction of Huangshan, A Three-Month Plan 167

The Huangshan area is vast, and there are many scenic spots. If we talk about unblocking traffic and widely building pavilions, it is not something that can be achieved urgently. Moreover, the terrain, geology, water sources, plants, etc. have not been explored by experts. Hasty construction is also not allowed by facts. Therefore, based on the most urgent needs, a preliminary construction plan has been formulated. Except for items 12 and 15, it is expected that all items will be completed from July 1st to September 30th of this year, laying the initial foundation and gradually seeking progress.

1. Repairing the original most important mountain roads and opening new earthen roads, 1,000 yuan.

2. Initial repair of roads and stone slope plank roads and small bridges in various places on the mountain, 4,000 yuan.

3. Adding and repairing guardrails on dangerous roads, 1,000 yuan.

4. Relocating and rebuilding Banshan Temple, 850 yuan.

5. Restoring Xiangfu Temple, 1,500 yuan.

6. Leveling the foundation of the Lotus Peak Top Temple, 150 yuan.

7. Setting up a viewing pavilion for Jiulong Waterfall, 500 yuan.

8. Building Shuangxi Pavilion at the confluence of Taohua and Zhusha streams, 1,000 yuan.

The above amount of 10,000 yuan is raised by Shiying personally.

9. Repairing Xinjiu Tangchi, 5,000 yuan.

10. Reorganizing scenic spots and historical sites inside and outside the mountain, 2,000 yuan.

11. Surveying fee for the first residential area (Taoyuan), more than 600 yuan.

The above amount of 7,600 yuan is allocated by the Anhui Provincial Government.

12. Construction expenses for roads and ditches in the first residential area, 16,000 yuan.

The above is allocated from the income of rented land prices.

13. Setting up a hotel, about 10,000 yuan, built by the Shanghai Bank and China Travel Service.

14. Jushilin, 5,000 yuan, is to be established by Shiying who will invite ten lay Buddhists, each responsible for 500 yuan.

15. After the surveying of the first residential area is completed and the route is demarcated, anyone may lease land according to the regulations and build a residence, but the drawings must be approved by the Huangshan Construction Committee's mountain office.

The Current Situation Under the Continuous Heat Wave: Asphalt on Roads Melts, Water Pipes Explode Due to Heat, Hospital Patients Surge, Rickshaw Pullers Faint 168

Yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 102 degrees, which was 1.7 degrees lower than the day before, but 17 degrees higher than the same day last year. Meteorological experts now believe that the heat wave in this city will gradually recede. Although it may return in the future, or even become hotter, it is expected that the maximum degree will not exceed the maximum degree in recent days in the next few days. According to meteorologists, the sudden heat was caused by a very dense layer of air sweeping in from the southwest, covering Shanghai and its surroundings, about 12,000 feet above the ground. This air layer is very mixed, so sunlight easily passes through. The heat emitted by the earth is usually scattered by various different air layers. Now, it suddenly increases the heat of the already very hot mixed layer. Therefore, it feels extraordinarily hot. For several days in a row, the asphalt-paved roads in the Concession have been melting due to excessive heat. Therefore, the Public Works Department of the Engineering Bureau has dispatched a large number of workers to spread sand on this type of road to facilitate pedestrians. The highest temperature on the surface of this type of road was 130 degrees on Sunday and increased to 140 degrees on Tuesday. It may have been even higher yesterday. The reason for the repeated increase is that the properties of asphalt retain heat. On Tuesday

At 1:00 p.m., when the sun was shining brightly, a 20-foot water pipe buried underground on Tiantong Road behind Gongji Hospital suddenly burst due to excessive heat on the ground. The water sprayed up to 80 feet, level with the roof of the hospital. Fortunately, no one was injured. Before long, the surrounding streets were two feet deep in water, forming a small lake. At that time, all kinds of vehicles detoured. The nearby playful children took advantage of this opportunity to bathe in the water. The water company dispatched workers to repair it that night. However, until the road is paved flat, Tiantong Road will temporarily stop traffic.

As a result of the continuous heat, the number of citizens suffering from heatstroke has increased sharply. At the Xizang Road Epidemic Hospital alone, there are already more than 300 patients. Not a few rickshaw pullers have fainted in the road due to heatstroke.

Fire in Xiafei Lane: A Girl Burned to Death. Is Keeping a Prostitute at Home an Omen of Bad Luck? The Girl Died Tragically with Her Abdomen Broken and Intestines Flowing Out 169

Wang Zuocai, alias Guoguang, a 44-year-old man from Ningbo, runs a construction business. He lives at No. 48 Xiafei Lane, No. 927 Xiafei Road, French Concession. He has a wife, Chen (37 years old, from Suzhou), and a 10-year-old eldest daughter named Gendi, and two sons, aged seven and five. He employs several servants. Because his business is successful, he has made a lot of profit and can be called well-off. Recently, Wang married a prostitute from a small garden as a concubine. Originally, they lived in two places. Later, in order to save expenses, Wang moved the concubine into his home to live with the wife. Before long, there were disagreements between them. Wang moved the concubine out to live separately, but the couple often quarreled because of this. Neighbors in the lane were superstitious and said that Wang's keeping a prostitute at home would inevitably bring bad luck. Wang laughed it off. Unexpectedly, the superstitious words came true. At around 3 a.m. yesterday, the electric wire installed at the entrance of the second-floor pavilion room door of Wang's house suddenly caught fire and exploded. His daughter Gendi, who was sleeping alone in the second-floor pavilion room, was the first to notice it. She shouted loudly that there was a fire. At that time, Wang and his wife, two sons, and servants heard the sound in the bedroom and panicked. They each ran away. His seven-year-old son, in a fit of anxiety, jumped out of the window, causing a fracture of his leg bones. However, Gendi, the daughter who first discovered the fire, could not escape because the flames filled the pavilion room. After Wang and the others escaped, they realized that their daughter had not escaped. They heard a faint cry. They rushed up to rescue her, but the fire in the pavilion room was so intense that there was nothing they could do. The girl was buried in the fire. After the fire brigade received the news, they immediately drove a leather belt car to the scene and took water to extinguish the fire. Only one pavilion room was burned down, and the rest of the house was fortunately preserved. Afterwards, firefighters dug out the body from the rubble pile in the pavilion room. It was charred and burned, with the abdomen broken and the intestines flowing out, broken limbs and feet, and the skull shattered. It was unbearable to look at. The police sent detectives to investigate the cause of the fire and then took the body to the autopsy room of the Tongren Fuyuan Branch. Wang Ren, the prosecutor appointed by the Second Special Court, and a forensic doctor arrived at the room at noon to examine the body and determined that the deceased had been burned to death before her death. The official asked Wang and his wife about the cause of the negligence, and then ordered the body to be handed over to the family members for burial.

Private Possession of Hand Grenades: Wang Yingchun Sentenced to a Fine of 200 Yuan; Hand Grenades Confiscated 170

Wang Yingchun, a native of Wuxi and employee of the hardware department of the New New Company, served in the First Brigade of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps during the outbreak of the Shanghai War in [blank] last year, distinguishing himself. After the ceasefire agreement was signed, Wang was discharged and returned to the company to continue his business. He brought with him two hand grenades, which he secretly stored in his clothes chest in the company's employee dormitory as mementos. He also removed the screw caps from the grenades to prevent danger. Recently, the company reported a theft of cigarettes and requested the police to investigate. Detective Yao Yuanlong and Detective Yang Peizhang went to the dormitory to search and found the two hand grenades in Wang's box. Wang Yingchun was taken to the police station and then sent to the First Special Court, where he was interrogated and detained. These facts have been reported in this newspaper. After Wang was arrested, the Shanghai Wuxi Native Association and the Shanghai Citizens' Federation of Nanjing Road, considering Wang to be a promising young man who had participated in national salvation efforts, and now facing legal trouble due to a mistake, rose to his defense. They hired three lawyers, Xue Dubi, Wang Chuanbi, and Lu Dingkui, to prepare his defense. Yesterday morning, the case was scheduled for a continued hearing. The three lawyers arrived in court on time. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated that the police had no new evidence since the adjournment and that the Western detective who conducted the search could testify to everything. The Western detective, Ma Yatou, testified that when they found the hand grenades on that day, the heads had indeed been removed, but the mechanisms were still in place and could still explode if something went wrong, although the danger was reduced. When questioned, Wang Yingchun stated that the heads of the hand grenades had been removed, but the gunpowder was still inside, and they would not explode if thrown on the ground. Judge Wu stated that while it was permissible to carry such hand grenades in the military camp, they should have been returned after discharge. Wang not only failed to return them but also concealed them without reporting it, which was dangerous. The defendant should not have kept them. Wang stated that they were mementos and had no other purpose. After lengthy arguments between the police lawyer and the defendant's lawyers, Judge Wu Tingqi ruled that Wang Yingchun possessed explosives without permission and imposed a fine of 200 yuan, and the two hand grenades were confiscated. Wang was granted permission to leave on bail of 200 yuan pending the appeal period, with Lawyer Xue responsible for his bail.

Nine Large Cans of Stinking Water Concealed 180,000 Red Pills; Seized by the North Station Road Police Station; Two Traffickers Arrested on the Spot 179

The poisonous atmosphere of red pills permeates the country, especially Shanghai. Although Chairman Chiang has ordered military and police agencies to strictly investigate, traffickers are still emerging one after another, and their methods are becoming increasingly varied. At about 3 p.m. the day before yesterday, when the Shanghai North Station on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway was about to open for through traffic to Ping, Zhong Jianhun, the police chief of the third section of the railway police department, suddenly saw two rattan boxes left near the ticket office of the station. He thought that they had been left behind by a hurried passenger and immediately inquired about them one by one. Before long, two men came forward to identify them, claiming that they had been left behind by their friends and that they had been specifically asked to come and claim them, and that the boxes contained clothes and disinfectant. The police chief, in order to verify this, invited them to the stationmaster's office at the North Station and opened the boxes together with the stationmaster on duty. The contents of the boxes were exactly as they had said, but then he saw that there were no business signs or labels on the nine large cans of disinfectant, which aroused great suspicion. He then tested them with an object and found that they were indeed stinking water, but the weight seemed inconsistent. He immediately declared that they must be opened for inspection. Unexpectedly, the two men strongly opposed this, appearing flustered. The stationmaster and police chief became even more suspicious and quickly used a knife to cut open the metal cans of stinking water. It was then that they saw two packages of red pills inside, with a small tube connecting to the top, which was used to store the stinking water, to cover people's eyes and ears. The police chief and others, having discovered the concealment, proceeded to open the remaining eight cans in the same way, and all contained red pills, totaling eighteen packages, weighing seventeen kilograms, each package containing 10,000 pills, for a total of 180,000 pills. The metal cans were twelve inches high and six inches square, so their capacity was quite large. The police chief then took the people and the goods to the police station. After questioning, one of them, Liu Tongquan, 36 years old, from Luoyang, Henan, vaguely denied trafficking in drugs. The other, Liu Tongchi, 43 years old, from Luoyang, Henan, claimed ignorance of the source of the drugs, saying only that he had been invited by Liu Tongquan to go to the North Station to help him carry his luggage, and therefore did not know what was in the boxes. After verifying the statements, the section chief considered that the case was a criminal one and sent the suspects and the red pills to the local court for handling, and reported it to the headquarters, instructing all police chiefs to cooperate with the municipal police to strengthen the search and suppression in order to eliminate the scourge of drugs.

Wang Zhentao Killed for Selling Inferior Goods; Instigator Wang Zhaocheng Arrested; Police Also Discover Two Other Cases Involving Wang; All Defendants Plead Not Guilty in Yesterday's Indictment 180

At 9:50 a.m. on November 18th of the year before last, Wang Zhentao, the owner of Maotai Xing Foreign Goods Store at No. 310 Xinzha Road, was shot and killed by members of the Iron-Blooded Anti-Traitor Corps for selling inferior goods. The police subsequently arrested the perpetrators Pan Hongsheng, Cao Songshou, and Tian Shuiyang, who were found guilty by the First Special District Court and sentenced to death and imprisonment. At 11:45 a.m. on the 15th of this month, detectives Ma Bingzhang and Wang Guangtian of the Jiaxing Road Police Station arrested Wang Zhaocheng, a native of Haining and the instigator of the case, in a house at No. 75 Anzhi Village, North Xizang Road, and sent him to the second criminal court. He pleaded not guilty and was detained for investigation. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu Yugui presided over the trial.厉志山, a lawyer of the Public Works Department, stated that the defendant had two additional cases during the adjournment: At 2:45 p.m. on the 24th of the same month, he went to a foreign goods store at No. 339 Hankou Road and shot and killed shareholder Wang Yirong, wounding Wu Zhuxuan, using the same method. The defendant was identified by the three perpetrators, Pan, Cao, and Tian, who were arrested by the police, as the person who supplied the bombs and pistols for the Xinzha Road shooting of Wang Tao. Now the three perpetrators can testify. When questioned, the defendant firmly denied it, saying that he was indeed working for Mr. Chen Lifu in the capital at the time. Previously, he worked for only twenty days in Shanghai, in the preparatory office of the Citizens' Volunteer Army's Northeast Engineering Team, with sixty-four people, and then went to Nanjing, as evidenced by newspapers. According to the perpetrator Pan Hongsheng, he knew the defendant during the January 28th Incident. The defendant was not involved in the Wang Zhentao case on Xinzha Road. Cao Songshou and Tian Shuiyang said that they did not know the defendant. His name was revealed by a released Hua surname, and they falsely accused him at the police station. The defendant Wang Zhaocheng was defended by three lawyers, Jiang Yiping, Jiang Chiping, and Sun Biwu. Judge Liu ordered him to be returned to custody for further verification.

Garrison Headquarters Prepares to Establish Shanghai Municipal Temporary Drug Rehabilitation Center; Opening Around July 10th 184

Since the Songhu Garrison Headquarters received Chairman Chiang's telegram strictly enforcing the drug prohibition order, Commander Wu Tiecheng has appointed Yu Youzhi, a technician of the Municipal Health Bureau and director of the Municipal South Clinic, to prepare for the establishment of the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau Temporary Drug Rehabilitation Center. The site has been surveyed and determined to be next to the orphanage opposite the Longhua Garrison Headquarters.

Commander Wu has allocated 10,000 yuan for start-up expenses, and the monthly recurring expenses will be 2,700 yuan thereafter. The method involves injecting a liquid, causing a blister to form on the skin. The doctor immediately extracts the toxic water and then makes another intramuscular injection. This method of using poison to fight poison can completely eliminate opium addiction in about a week. Then, the center issues a certificate of abstinence, and the Garrison Headquarters releases the addict after taking a guarantee. If there is a relapse, the addict will be arrested and executed.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Notifies All Industries that National Goods Must Be Marked with Trademarks for Easy Identification by Purchasers 186

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the trade associations of all industries yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you on behalf of the Women's National Goods Year Movement Committee, which was recently established. We are actively promoting national goods and sparing no effort to fulfill our mission of the Women's National Goods Year. However, due to the social custom of often buying foreign goods, the results of the promotion over the past six months have been limited. Recently, our committee convened a joint meeting of the Economic Work Committee and the Design Committee to discuss how to continue the promotion for the benefit of the implementation. It was agreed that national goods sellers and consumers must have a spirit of comprehensive cooperation in order to achieve the actual effect of promoting national goods. The daily necessities needed by families are often filled with foreign goods, and it is difficult to identify the marks of national goods manufacturers. As a result, once they are purchased, they may be found to be inferior goods. It is requested that all major companies mark all kinds of national goods with the manufacturer and its trademark, so that customers can easily identify them. We are writing to your association to persuade all companies and manufacturers to adopt this practice as soon as possible." The council believes that the proposal of marking all kinds of national goods with the manufacturer's name and trademark is indeed for the sake of easy identification. However, the council believes that foreign companies have set up factories in China under treaties, and the factory names are only Chinese characters, so it is not possible to judge which is a foreign factory. Therefore, it is best to also print the factory address and the names of the factory owner or directors on the packaging of the goods, so that people can know at a glance that they are products of a Chinese factory. We are sending this letter to inform you and hope that your association will pass it on to the factories of your members and implement it in a practical manner, so as to avoid difficulties in identification and make it easy for counterfeiters to fake the products.

Rent Reduction Dispute in Jinyu Fang 191

Jinyu Fang in Dajing Lane, inside Xiaobeimen, is an old-fashioned building with one floor and one bottom. It was slightly repaired in 1933, and the rent was increased by 16 yuan per unit (from 25 yuan to 40 yuan). The rent of nearby houses before and after is only 13 yuan per unit, and the highest is no more than 20 yuan. The rent is the highest in the Xiaobeimen to Jiumudi area. Due to the economic downturn, the tenants of the Fang could no longer afford this huge rent. They organized a rent reduction committee in January and jointly requested the landlord to reduce the rent in writing. Not only did the landlord not agree, but he also used severe oppressive means and asked the lawyer's court to sue. Therefore, the tenants of the Fang had no choice but to discuss together and stop paying rent. Before the rent reduction was resolved, they temporarily stored the monthly rent in the Ximen Shanghai Bank for public certification. On June 9, Mr. Li took the initiative to mediate and agreed to reduce the rent. In order to settle the matter, the tenants of the Fang agreed to his request. Unexpectedly, the landlord demanded that Mr. Jin, who was enthusiastic about public welfare, be ordered to move out before the rent could be reduced. Therefore, Mr. Li was unable to mediate. Yesterday, all the tenants held a general meeting and decided that if a fair solution could not be reached, they would stick to their original intention and insist on it, regardless of any sacrifice.

In an instant, it spread to the left and right neighbors, with thick smoke and bright flames. The fire brigade heard the alarm and rushed to the scene to put out the fire. Tailor Commits Suicide Due to Poverty 193

Ding Yinshan, a native of Shaoxing who specializes in tailoring at Longji Clothing Store at Nos. 129-131 Fujian Road, 45 years old, suddenly cut his throat with a sharp razor at 7:15 a.m. yesterday and committed suicide. When people found out, he was rushed to Renji Hospital, but he died on the way. The store owner, Xie Changlin, reported it to the Laozha Police Station, and the body was taken to the autopsy office for examination. As for the reason for Ding's suicide, according to his colleagues in the store, Ding had been working in the store for five years, and his monthly salary was only about 20 yuan. He had always been extremely frugal. However, recently, Ding's son and daughter-in-law all moved to Shanghai, and all the expenses had to be borne by Ding completely, which made Ding feel economically pressured and resort to this tactic.

Painting by Shuangyu Taoist 194

Yesterday, while dining at a friend's residence, this reporter saw a landscape painting hanging on the wall, with heavy and vigorous brushstrokes, unlike the work of a modern person. It was signed Shuangyu Taoist. When asked who painted it, the host said, "This is the painter Tang Dingzhi, whom you praised many years ago. I met him in Beijing more than ten years ago through Zhao Shengbobo. He is a very upright person and has a passion for tea. He has come to Shanghai every year since last year, and he often talks with me about the origins of ancient inscriptions and calligraphy until late at night. People only know that he is good at landscapes, pine trees, plum blossoms, bamboos, and rocks, but they do not know that his authentic cursive script and Han official script are almost indistinguishable from those of the masters of the late Ming and early Qing dynasties. His name is Di, the great-grandson of the Duke of Zhenmin and the grandson of Mr. Yue Min. He can be said to have carried on the family's learning." I asked what Shuangyu meant. The host said, "I will introduce him to you and treat you to wine another day."

This combined issue sells for 50 cents, and a full year (four issues) costs 1.20 yuan. Stamps are accepted at full value. Those wishing to subscribe can contact the association at 131 Museum Road, Shanghai.

Reading Q&A

[P Further Discussion on Building a Mass Language

Linguistics │ Answer to Mr. Wang Sheng-san │

Since we published an article "How to Build a Mass Language Literature," many readers have raised their opinions to us. For example, why is the mass language anti-classical Chinese, and at the same time anti-vernacular? What is the standard language of the mass language? We believe that these questions really need to be raised again for discussion.

We once said, "The current mass language movement is anti-classical Chinese, and at the same time, it is anti-bureaucratic comprador vernacular," because "the mass language is as opposed to vernacular as it is to classical Chinese." Although there is nothing wrong with this opinion in principle, it is a bit vague in saying it, and it does not precisely delineate the differences between them or correctly point out the unity of opposition between vernacular and mass language, which has led to misunderstandings among readers, who think that opposing vernacular is equal to opposing classical Chinese.

That is not our intention!

The development of language and writing, like social development, has its own specific procedures. If we want to understand how mass language and vernacular oppose each other and how they are unified, we can only understand it from the process of language development. We say that the mass language is anti-vernacular, because the vernacular movement has not completed its own task and achieved the success of "consistency between speech and writing." On the contrary, it has taken the road of surrendering to "literary language," becoming an obstacle to the development of language and writing. Just look at the popular vernacular writing now│not Blue-Green Mandarin, but a disguised form of the eight-legged essay (the so-called "quotation style") and there is a very large distance from the masses. Those young writers who sarcastically and abusively write "Damn it" and "Mom's" into literary works are no different from Wang Maozu's promotion of classical Chinese in terms of opposing the mass language.

However, saying this does not mean that ··anti-vernacular is equal to anti-classical Chinese, or that anti-vernacular, like anti-classical Chinese, has the meaning of denying all vernacular. No. We oppose vernacular in order to further oppose classical Chinese, and in order to further guarantee the victory of obtaining "consistency between speech and writing." In the "May Fourth" era, the mass language movement was included in the vernacular movement. Our opposition to vernacular does not deny the part that vernacular has achieved in the entire language movement; it declared the "death penalty of literary language" and pointed out the inevitability of "consistency between speech and writing" in the future. Therefore, in the current stage of building a mass language, we oppose vernacular's departure from the masses, but we cannot but critically accept everything in vernacular that is close to the mass language. After all, vernacular is different from classical Chinese, and vernacular is, after all, closer to the mass language.

So, what in vernacular should we accept? What is the standard language of the mass language? This question cannot be answered mechanically.

Language is not static, but is constantly changing with the progress of social life. The emergence of vernacular in the May Fourth era was also the starting point of the mass language. In this process, in the development of opposition between vernacular and mass language, the mass language gradually grows, while the vernacular of wealthy merchants and compradors becomes weaker and more exposed to its reactionary nature. If we deny the existence and development of the mass language in vernacular, we are no different from denying the meaning of the entire language movement, or even the cultural movement. Not to mention anything else, if we take the vernacular before and after the May Fourth period and compare it with the general vernacular now, and compare the vernacular of the remnants of the past with the works of mass literature writers, we can know which is closer to the masses. What is meant here by being close to the masses refers not only to language, but also to content. The masses here do not refer to the conservative masses, but to the progressive masses). This development of language and writing is gradual rather than sudden (the May Fourth vernacular movement can be said to be sudden), so we cannot easily see its form of development or point out a few works that can truly serve as the standard of mass language literature.

Answering the question of what is the standard language of the mass language in this way can lead to the same correct conclusion. Some people think that the standard language of the mass language should be the popular Mandarin, while others think it should be the vernacular popular on ships and trains. They all regard language as a static thing, and regard the development of language as unrelated to all aspects of the real life of the masses. They only see these elements that constitute the mass language, and mistakenly regard one element as the whole. We are now building a mass language literature, and we can certainly presuppose a standard language, but this standard language cannot be regarded as the future mass language, but only as the basis for this movement. The mass language grows in the real life of the masses. Mr. Xia Jizun said that farm women also shout "revolution," but it is not mass language, but during the Northern Expedition, farm women in parts of Jiangxi, Hunan, and Guangdong really could talk about revolution, and we cannot but say that it was mass language. At present, language and writing still have great differences in themselves. What is understandable to read may not be understandable to hear, and what is understandable to hear may not be understandable to read. It is permissible for us to adopt a certain language as the standard language for this movement (this requires the efforts of linguists and sociologists). However, it is obvious that this is not the main point. We believe that the main tasks of building the mass language at the present stage are:

(1) To improve the shape-meaning characters and gradually turn them into phonetic characters, breaking the fundamental differences between language and writing;

(2) To improve the lives, culture, and enhance the vocabulary of the masses, so that the language of the masses and the general cultural development tend to be in a consistent pace.

Detailed explanations of these two points will be discussed later.

To Cultivate Submissive and Enslaved Normal School Talents

Scheduled to Open This September

(Northeast News Agency Changchun Telegram) Considering that medium and higher level enslavement schools are still lacking in the pseudo- "Xing'an Province," and that Mongolian scholars have traditionally tended to go to Beijing, Shanghai, Nanjing, and other places to receive education in China, which is very detrimental to its enslavement policy and aggressive tactics, Japan recently incited the pseudo-Xing'an General Office to establish an Xing'an Academy in Wangyemiao, the former banner of Xike in the southern branch province, directly under the pseudo-Xing'an General Office, in order to cultivate submissive slave professions and enslavement normal school talents with its so-called "Wangdao Thought" and "National Foundation through Agriculture and Industry," so as to prevent students from studying in other places and complete its purpose of aggression.
