Zhou Fo Hai Discusses the Implementation of Secondary Education in Jiangsu (Part 3) 218

I also have some opinions on this matter, and I must take this opportunity to explain them to everyone. In the past, many students created by middle schools could neither pursue further education nor possess productive skills, and were merely middle-class vagrants in society, adding a floating force to society and making it more chaotic. In order to remedy this shortcoming, we should promote vocational education or life education to cultivate students' productive skills so that they can live independently. On the negative side, this reduces the floating population in society; on the positive side, it increases the productive forces in society. In theory and principle, no one can disagree with this. However, looking at the current production environment in China, all production industries have not yet developed. Whether vocational school students will have a way out in the future is also a major question. According to the statistics of this province in the 21st year, the total number of vocational high school graduates in the province was 218. Except for 40 students from the business department of Shanghai Middle School whose reports were not available, only 99 people were employed, accounting for about 56% of the total. There are still 40% who cannot find a job. Although a small number of them pursue further education, many are still unemployed. Now that there are not many vocational school graduates, this phenomenon already exists. If vocational education is expanded in the future, and the number of graduates increases day by day, wouldn't this be another major problem? In addition to making the curriculum of each vocational school practical, training serious, and cultivating students' scientific minds and the skills of farmers and workers to meet the needs of social enterprises, I also ask that the province's various business institutions can accommodate as many vocational school graduates as possible. Because the talents trained with provincial funds are certainly for private enterprises, but if they can be used by the public, it is even more cost-effective. If the talents trained with provincial funds cannot gain a foothold in the province's various business institutions, it seems to deviate slightly from the original intention of provincial schools. This is a hope that I have based on the narrow employment prospects of vocational students in the past. In addition, there is another point, which can also be said to be a feeling that I have arisen because of talking about restricting the expansion of middle schools. Generally, people think that there are not many secondary school students in China. According to the statistics of the Ministry of Education, the number of secondary school students in China per 10,000 people is only 11, which is only one-fiftieth of that in Germany. The number of secondary school students in other countries is also ten times or twenty-thirty times that of China. It can be seen that secondary education in China, in another sense, seems to be allowed to expand naturally and should not be restricted in any way. However, I believe that the number of secondary school students in China at this time cannot be compared with other countries. Elementary education in various countries has almost reached the point of universalization, so they can further plan for the popularization of secondary education. Human culture is endless, so education is also endless. In the past, many European and American countries believed that four years of compulsory education was enough, and adult literacy education only taught the most basic reading, writing, and arithmetic. Now, the general trend is to extend the length of compulsory education to six or eight years, and the curriculum of adult literacy education, according to the literacy education promoted by the British Labor Education Association and various universities, is almost equal to that of universities in terms of high curriculum standards. In the future, the general trend may be to make secondary education compulsory, and secondary education in various countries will be completely popularized one day, and it will not only account for a certain number of people per 10,000 population. As for China, elementary education is still far from universalization. What we should strive for today is the development of elementary education. We can only gradually expand secondary education according to the needs of the environment. After elementary education is completely popularized, we can further expand secondary education. We must not ignore the foundation and compete with various countries across levels. We cannot but admit this inevitable fact. Therefore, I hope that all people with aspirations for education in the province will recognize this fact, start from the root, and strive to develop primary school education, instead of being ambitious and wanting to run middle schools at every turn. According to what I know, the number of private middle schools in Zhejiang accounts for 49% of the total number of middle schools in the province, and the number of private primary schools accounts for more than 50% of the total number of primary schools in the province. Private middle schools in Jiangsu account for about 50% of the total number of middle schools in the province, while the number of private primary schools only accounts for more than 9% of the total number of primary schools in the province. Comparing the two, we cannot help but admire the correct vision of people in Zhejiang who run private schools. In the future, people in Jiangsu who are enthusiastic about running private schools should not run middle schools, but try their best to run primary schools. This is my greatest wish, and I think it is also the common wish of the people of our province. End.

Wimbledon Tennis, Day Two 238

Three of Four Japanese Players Eliminated

No Other Surprises; Women's Singles Begin

(Reuters, London, 26th) Intermittent rain and cloudy skies prevailed today at the Wimbledon tennis tournament. The men's singles competition continued without any major upsets, although three of the four Japanese players have been eliminated. Attendance reached over 6,000.

Three Japanese Players Eliminated 239

Miki Lost to Turnbull: In the second week of the men's singles, Miki was defeated by Turnbull of Australia, 6-3, 6-1. Miki was completely out of sorts, unable to answer Turnbull's cannonball serves, often hitting the ball out of bounds or into the net. His performance was subpar.

Fujikura Lost to Haberl 240

Fujikura was eliminated by the giant Englishman Haberl after a five-set match. Haberl won 6-4, 3-6, 1-6, 7-5, 6-4. Haberl had previously defeated Cochet of France and Morpurgo of Italy at Wimbledon. Today, Haberl's performance reached its peak, hitting from the baseline and seizing opportunities to come to the net. Fujikura remained on the baseline. The match was briefly interrupted due to rain.

Nishimura Eliminated by Siba 241

Nishimura, the third Japanese player to be eliminated, lost to Siba of Czechoslovakia in five sets, 8-6, 4-6, 8-6, 2-6, 9-7. In the first and third sets, Nishimura led 5-4 and was only one point away from winning when a sudden downpour occurred. After the match resumed, Nishimura's performance plummeted. The sun reappeared in the fourth set, but Nishimura was out of form. The fifth set became a test of endurance, with Nishimura leading 4-1, but Siba caught up to 5-4. At this point, Nishimura was exhausted.

Yamagishi, the Only Remaining Hope 242

The only remaining Japanese player, Yamagishi, easily defeated Le Sueur of France, a left-handed player, 6-1, 6-1, 6-3. Yamagishi's deep shots to the corners forced his opponent to run constantly, and his volleys were excellent, earning him much applause.

Important British and American Players Win 243

Lott, an American Davis Cup player, defeated Stefani of Italy 3-6, 6-3, 6-4, 6-4. Wood defeated Emer of Switzerland in four sets, and Shields defeated Rontlet (France).

Henman defeated Williams, the non-playing captain of the American Davis Cup team, 6-2, 6-2, 6-0. Austin also won in straight sets against Taeckel of Germany.

Crawford defeated Haeckel of Germany, 6-2, 6-3, 3-6, 6-4. Jones, a beautiful young woman from Cambridge University, defeated Hughes of Britain.

Menruel of Czechoslovakia easily defeated Shansiang of France. The young Frenchman Maillan defeated his compatriot Brunnion, and Hecht of Czechoslovakia defeated Mael of Spain.

Shen Bao National Products Weekly

Words of Contribution

Go to the Interior 246

— Yang An

The bankruptcy of the rural economy in the interior is evident, and the weakness of the farmers' purchasing power is apparent. Shanghai, a hub of commerce and industry, is also suffering as a result, with its decline becoming increasingly noticeable. The financial sector is burdened with large amounts of capital and struggles to find suitable investment opportunities. The domestic goods industry is plagued by stockpiles and sluggish sales, leading to the hardship of stagnant inventory. Even more unfortunate is the existence of specialized talent without opportunities for development, leaving many heroes with no place to utilize their abilities. Given the state of China, the only path forward is to implement the "Go to the Interior" principle, which is essential to alleviate current hardships. Zhang Gongquan has advocated this principle to the nation. He recently traveled to Sichuan, known as the "Land of Abundance," for an inspection and tour lasting a month, and returned with great admiration. He believes that Sichuan is the wealthiest region in China, and it offers the most promising opportunities for the people to forge new paths. The people of Sichuan are determined to abandon the old notion of "Sichuan for the people of Sichuan" and embrace capital, goods, and technology from other provinces to develop this exceptionally rich region, aiming to rival England and the United States. This is the sincere desire of China's domestic goods industry, which must find ways to realize it. Zhang also stated that Sichuan's annual income is 120 million yuan, six times that of Jiangsu, China's wealthiest province, highlighting its immense wealth. Sichuan absorbs a large volume of goods annually, with cotton yarn alone accounting for approximately 120,000 bales. Sichuan people are major consumers of other domestic goods as well. Therefore, if we are to discuss domestic goods, we must not forget Sichuan. Zhang strongly encourages the domestic goods industry to jointly visit Sichuan for on-site observations and to establish trade connections. The reporter deeply sympathizes with this and sincerely hopes that leaders of the domestic goods industry will promptly organize a Sichuan Commerce and Industry Inspection Group to conduct research and share their findings. Organizing a Sichuan National Products Exhibition to stimulate the purchasing power of Sichuan people would also greatly benefit the progress and promotion of domestic goods. The reporter strongly urges leaders of various manufacturers to consider this proposal.

Talks on National Products

Bureaucrats and National Products 247

— Xiao Bai

In a previous issue of this publication, there was an article by Mr. Baling titled "National Products and Prostitutes." He argued that national products are dignified, while prostitutes are base. However, he further stated that if a respectable woman abandons the use of domestic goods and instead promotes foreign products, she is even more shameful than a prostitute. This made me consider the relationship between "bureaucrats and national products," and I would like to discuss their close connection in detail.

"Aiming high and admiring vanity" is inherent in human nature worldwide. We can find examples throughout our own history. When Guo Linzong of the Han dynasty encountered rain, he inadvertently folded the corner of his headscarf. People at the time imitated him, deliberately folding their own headscarves to take pride in it, calling it the "Linzong scarf." When Zeng Guofan served as the Governor-General of Liangjiang, he used a large, coarse palm-leaf fan to cool himself during the hottest days. The entire staff and people of Nanjing followed suit, abandoning delicate silk fans in favor of palm-leaf fans. This phenomenon is not unique to our country; it also occurs in European and American nations. Shortly after the end of the European War, when US President Wilson visited Europe, he rode in a car with the Queen of England. In haste, he inadvertently folded his cuff. Before the day was over, people throughout London were competing to fold their cuffs in imitation, demonstrating the significant influence of such actions.

Therefore, we can deeply understand that the actions of the upper class have a significant impact on the customs of our national population and the transformation of social trends. If they could strongly advocate "using domestic goods and rejecting foreign goods," taking the lead and setting an example for the public, the results would undoubtedly be more effective. However, what is the reality? It is far from our ideal. Past events have often revealed that large quantities of imported luxury goods are primarily consumed by those in political circles. Some bureaucrats, wearing foreign clothes, stand on the podium, preaching about saving the nation through domestic goods, while their actions contradict their words. Their shame is even greater than that of prostitutes.

Recently, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek launched the "New Life Movement," which includes the principle of using domestic goods, demonstrating its importance. Since he issued this call, there has been a nationwide response, with many eager to follow his lead. For example, Han Fuju, Chairman of Shandong Province, and Lu Diping, Chairman of Zhejiang Province, have made efforts to promote domestic goods and serve as role models for the public. If the entire political circle of our nation can thoroughly awaken from now on, embrace determination, and lead the public to take practical action, starting with those in political and academic circles, and then extending to the business community, and setting domestic goods as the standard for clothing and all consumption in the New Life Movement, then the future of domestic goods will be bright and predictable.

A Study of the National Goods Purchasing Competition 248

— Ding Xing

In recent days, the newspapers have been promoting a very new term, which is "National Goods Purchasing Competition." This competition is sponsored by the China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperation Association and organized by the China National Goods Company. Their purpose is to test the enthusiasm of the Chinese people for using national goods. The competition will last for three weeks, from June 24th to July 14th. It is divided into three types of competitions: total competition, weekly competition, and daily competition. The method is to register at the competition office with invoices (excluding special goods and wholesale invoices) for purchases of products from various departments of the China National Goods Company that are worth more than ten points ││i.e., ten yuan.││ If you prefer to participate in the daily competition, then you can participate in the daily competition. For example, the first prize winner of the first day of the daily competition was 299.20 points ││i.e., purchases worth 299 yuan and 2 jiao.││ The first prize of the daily competition is a 100-yuan China National Goods Company gift certificate. The first prize of the weekly competition is a 200-yuan China National Goods Company gift certificate. The first prize of the total competition is a 500-yuan China National Goods Company gift certificate.

Now, let's take the example of the first prize winner of the first day, who won a 100-yuan prize for purchasing 299 yuan and 2 jiao worth of goods. It is undoubtedly a sacrifice for them. So why are they willing to make such a sacrifice? It is nothing more than to encourage the Chinese people to buy more national goods, so as to avoid the outflow of profits.

However, some people say, "I don't need so many things, and I don't have that much purchasing power. Although their prize amount is so high, it still doesn't benefit me at all, does it?" Because of his question, I did some research to answer him: "It is true that an individual's purchasing power is weak. I think you can join forces with your colleagues. Isn't there more than 500 people in your company? Let's say there are 300 people. In the summer, there are necessities such as undershirts and towels. ││This is a common example.││ At one yuan per person, you get 300 yuan. By participating in the daily competition with this amount, you can get a 100-yuan gift certificate. The 100 yuan can be exchanged for goods. If you take the usual purchase example, isn't this equal to an extra income?" My friend heard this and said happily, "Wonderful! Wonderful!"

This is an example of many people buying together. There are also consumer cooperatives, small capital firms, school shops, military units, agencies, etc. In normal times, they have to buy various goods for sale, or to give away as gifts. You can take this opportunity to buy from them in large quantities, and there will be extra income from the large amount of prizes. Isn't this a best opportunity? Moreover, if you don't win in the daily competition, you can participate in the weekly competition. If you don't win in the weekly competition, you can still participate in the total competition. If you don't win in the total competition, you can get a gift based on the total value of the invoices. Therefore, their slogan is "Winners of the competition get prizes, and those who do not win the competition get gifts."

Finally, I think their strategy this time is excellent and superior, and they are not afraid to sacrifice. This spirit is worthy of praise from the Chinese people. I think although Shanghai is a market full of foreign goods, after such a surge, some dreamers will awaken to some extent!

Discussion on National Products

How to Educate Children to Promote National Products? 249

— Dao

I believe in Ms. Ellen Key's words: "The twentieth century is the world of children." However, in the world of children, there is an urgent need for child-like teachers to educate them, just like a gardener irrigates an unopened rosebud. Plump fragrance and intoxicating color require strong assistance and diligent cultivation to unfold their color and fragrance. The importance of childhood can be seen in general.

However, innocent children have delicate minds, immature thoughts, and are most receptive to imitation and have strong memories. At this time, how can teachers educate children to get on the right track? It is an important key. Children mostly regard the words and deeds of teachers as vivid pictures, lively movies, and engraved words. They spend all day together, influenced by what they see and hear, and learn by example.

This year is the year of the child. At the same time, the situation of promoting national products is also showing a thriving phenomenon. In this period, if teachers impart knowledge of the nation to children, and instill the principles of promoting national products in them, the impression is extremely profound and the relationship is also very important. To solidify children's pure thoughts of promoting national products, to create children's basic concept of using national products, it all depends on this. As for the teachers, "How to educate children to promote national products?" It is indeed a question worth discussing, and it is also a huge responsibility that teaching should bear. I think we should pay attention to the following points:

First, we must adopt teaching materials that promote national products. The teaching materials for educating children should pay attention to the manufacturing of national products, the introduction of national products, the clarification of the theory of saving the country with national products, the revelation of the methods of promoting national products, and the guidance on the advantages and disadvantages of promoting the use of national products and the use of foreign goods.

Second, we must teach the methods of promoting national products. Promoting the use of national products is of course important for both consumption and production. Teaching methods must also pay attention to the use of both hands and brains, and the combination of teaching and learning. In normal times, we should instill more knowledge of agriculture and industry to children, guide children to make prototype handicrafts of agricultural and industrial products, and especially lead children to visit national goods factories, national goods stores, national goods exhibition halls, national goods exhibitions, etc. to broaden their horizons.

Third, we must implement the discipline of promoting national products. Whether direct or indirect, tangible or intangible, discipline can cultivate children's habit of using national products. For example, uniforms should all be made of national cloth, stationery should all be bought from domestic manufacturers, and national goods consumer cooperatives, national goods lecture groups, and national goods sales teams should be organized.

Spring and Autumn

Records of Lingering Fragrance 252

— Original by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

However, despite the busy work, there were never any mistakes such as delaying the serving of dishes or placing bowls and plates upside down. Don't underestimate them, readers! Their movements were truly somewhat militarized! When it came time to start the fire, the fifty cooks in Group C would all begin simultaneously. Because everyone's techniques were identical, the coal balls in the stove would ignite at the same time, and the temporary short chimneys would also be removed at the same time. The most interesting sight was when the fifty cooks in Group C bent over together, each using a palm-leaf fan to fan the flames, resembling the synchronized and methodical movements of boatmen on sampan boats.

Although these cooks were divided into Groups A, B, and C based on their positions, their attire was uniformly equal. They all dressed like eunuchs in the palace, except with white cloth sleeves. Therefore, in these four carriages used as temporary kitchens, the colors were as bright and eye-catching as in the other carriages.

In the past, people, regardless of their wealth or status, did not pay much attention to the cleanliness of the kitchen. The Empress Dowager, however, was different. When she was in the palace, she would often personally inspect the kitchen, so it was always kept very clean. This time, although the temporary kitchen set up on the train was small, cleanliness was still highly emphasized. I dare say that I have never seen such a clean kitchen. Even the floor was scrubbed so clean that there was no dust at all, almost clean enough to eat off of.

Two meals each day were designated as "formal meals," during which the full set of one hundred dishes had to be served properly. In addition to these two formal meals, there were also two smaller meals. Since they were called smaller meals, they were naturally not as elaborate as the formal meals. However, the Empress Dowager never allowed them to be too casual, so each smaller meal still consisted of at least twenty dishes, and usually around forty or fifty. (69)

"Buzzing" Small Talk 253

— Hu Chenzhou

My small, rectangular nest has two windows of different sizes facing north. In front is the tennis court of the owner of the three-story western-style building over there, which breeds a large number of grass mosquitoes. Every night, thousands upon thousands of flying generals invade my room. Because my abode is not equipped with "wire mesh" like theirs, I am completely surrounded by them! They buzz and shout, attacking my entire body, leaving not a single piece of skin intact... It's no good sitting, and it's no good standing; I can't write. Thinking of Pi Rixiu's poem "Mosquitoes"... "Hiding, gathering like thunder, secretly sucking blood without satisfaction; if Heaven is not fair, tiny creatures will be taught to eat flesh. Poor scholars have no red gauze, enduring hardship, lying in thatched huts, why seek fatty food, with no grain in the stomach!" I hate them even more!

I remember Fang Xiaoru, who called himself Tiantaishan Sheng in the Ming Dynasty, once wrote a "Mosquito Dialogue." He described the mosquitoes... " ...like ants like flies, greedy mouths full belly, red and round..." He said that mosquitoes are as big as flies, which is probably the same as the "megalomania" of ordinary literati; let's not worry about it. Look, he used the words of his boy to tell a great truth..." ... Moreover, things eat people, and people eat things, they are different, it is still ok to say. Even mosquitoes are still cautious and afraid, not daring to show their shape in the daytime, peeking at people's invisibility, taking advantage of people's tiredness, and then asking for it. Now there are people of the same kind, who drink the same soup, raise wives and raise children, and the clothes and appearances are all the same. They are in the same category during the day and harass them, sucking their fat and smashing their brains, making them hungry, stumbling in the wilderness, wandering on the road, and the sounds of calling out to the sky are connected, and no one cares about them... "

Alas, according to this, people are not as good as mosquitoes, so why should I hate them!

Random Notes from Jade Ewer 254

— Qian Da from Jiangnan

Mr. Jia Mingzhou, Chief of Staff of the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army's General Commander Wang Delin's forces, came south on assignment to handle the post-war affairs of the families of the generals under his command. I met him at a banquet arranged by a friend. Mr. Jia is gentle and refined, and speaks with wit and elegance, not at all like a military man. Halfway through the meal, he spoke freely about the anti-Japanese situation of the volunteer army, his words filled with fervor and tragedy, moving and heart-wrenching, causing a patriotic feeling to arise spontaneously in people. It has been a long time since the public has heard the sound of resistance against Japan, and the newspapers rarely publish news about the volunteer army. The three characters "Volunteer Army" are almost forgotten. Who still remembers that thousands of miles away, there are still some patriotic heroes fighting bloody battles with the Japanese invaders day and night, hoping to recover the lost territory for their motherland? Mr. Jia spoke about an incident where his troops used burning chili peppers to repel enemy planes, which was very interesting. The enemy's superiority over us lies in their large number of planes and cannons, not in the combat effectiveness of their soldiers. The volunteer army mostly hides in deep mountains and remote valleys, forming a dispersed battle line, precisely because they fear being targeted by planes. One day, hundreds of soldiers from Wang's volunteer army happened to gather together, unexpectedly a large squadron of enemy planes suddenly arrived, having detected them. At this critical moment, their danger was unparalleled. Suddenly, someone, in a moment of desperation, came up with a brilliant idea, ordering everyone to collect countless chili peppers and pile them into a large heap, setting it on fire. In an instant, smoke and flames filled the sky, and the spicy fumes spread everywhere. This move was unexpected by the enemy. The people in the planes, upon smelling it, could not help but have their noses run and tears flow, unable to endure it. They were all shocked and quickly steered the planes away, thus the siege was lifted. However, they never figured out what the volunteer army had released. Everyone at the table laughed when Mr. Jia spoke about this. Mr. Jiang Baili, a senior military expert, was also present and couldn't help but smile, saying, "This can truly be called homemade poison gas."

According to a friend, among the families of Northeast anti-Japanese generals staying in Shanghai, there are many wives of high-ranking military officers. If they were in China proper, they would all be broad-minded ladies riding in cars, eating fancy meals, and being fawned upon by thousands. It is only because their husbands' blood is too hot that they reluctantly abandoned their families, disregarded everything, and willingly fought a desperate battle with the enemy, which led them to drift to a foreign land, destitute and without a home, relying solely on the relief of charitable organizations to barely make a living. Their situation is just like that of refugees. And looking north towards their homeland, their old homes have fallen into the hands of foreign invaders. Some people listen to the radio, while others appreciate the scenery thousands of miles away. Their husbands are still fighting for their lives in the midst of gunfire, and there must be not a few who have become figures in their spring boudoir dreams. This kind of feeling, even for an outsider to put themselves in their shoes, is still unbearable, let alone for those who have personally experienced it?

The Philosophy of Clothing 256

— Zui Chi Sheng

In today's contradictory society, the rich can pretend to be poor. It doesn't matter if their clothes are a bit old, and there are many benefits to it. 1) Pretending to be poor avoids the covetous eyes of kidnappers and thieves. 2) It avoids being asked for loans and spending money. Ordinary poor friends who don't know the truth will think you're one of them. Naturally, they will shy away and seek someone else. 3) As long as you have money, people will come to flatter you. Pretending to be poor will make many people praise you, saying you have "admirable frugality." Zhuangzi used to say, "Great wisdom appears foolish, great skill appears clumsy." I'll change it to, "Great fatness appears thin, great wealth appears poor." This is the way for the rich to live in the world!

But the poor must put on the airs of the rich. If you have a high or low position and are short on money, even if you have no food for the next day, you must pay attention to your appearance and wear beautiful clothes. Otherwise, if you are dressed in rags, even if you are "learned and talented," people will still look down on you. They will even give you a cold shoulder and call you a poor ghost. When you go out to visit friends, you will "always be obstructed" and be given the cold shoulder. Even your career will be severely affected. "Only valuing clothes and not the person" is an unbreakable saying. As for if you are a "pretty boy" who wants to chase after the ladies, you must study the decorations even more. A modern suit is indispensable. Naturally, there will be members of the opposite sex who will favor you. "The poor pretending to be rich, the rich pretending to be poor," this is the "philosophy of clothing."

Random Talk

Early Summer Notes 257

— Zhu Lu

——A few cross-sections of Suzhou——

Making Things Difficult for Celebrities

Ever since Master Taiyan, the great scholar of textual criticism, bought a house and settled down on Jinfan Creek, becoming a rentier in a Western-style house, the celebrities of Suzhou who admired the Master, or the Master's disciples, had something to do. With the high mountain in sight, there was a way to admire him. Either they went to him for instruction or they hosted a banquet to welcome him. The Master originally came to Suzhou to escape the hustle and bustle of Shanghai, but after arriving in Suzhou, his seats were always full of guests and his cups were never empty. Even the telephone that was hastily installed overnight kept ringing all day long, making it difficult for the Master to achieve his wish to escape the noise. The other day, the Master was invited by a disciple to a banquet at the Langcang Yaji. When the wine was half-drunk, the host asked him to compose a poem on the spot to leave an immortal memorial of the grand event. The Master was originally a famous artist, and he dashed off a four-line ancient poem in one go, but the celebrities accompanying him felt greatly embarrassed! If they did, since there were pearls and jade in front of them, they would certainly not be able to write any wonderful words. If they didn't, it would be difficult to refuse the host's elegant intention. For a moment, the celebrities at the table felt uneasy! Buzzing sounds arose, and the cups and dishes were silent. But the next day, the news of this grand gathering and the Master's wonderful words were prominently published in the newspaper to highlight Suzhou's culture!

"Bone-Corroding, Soul-Melting" Negotiations

In this year of economic depression, especially in these months of May and June, the general business situation is even more blatantly showing the signs of economic depression! Especially the empty-stomach gaming industry. The two Beijing opera houses in Suzhou, one inside and one outside the city, have successively stopped performing, and the movie theaters are also doing poor business, so they have to bring in some song and dance troupes to attract customers with fleshiness, and publish deceptive words such as "Stark Naked" in the newspaper advertisements. In fact, under the inspection of the Public Entertainment Review Committee and the Public Security Bureau, a truly naked woman will never be found in a Suzhou theater or on the screen. However, the other day, it led to negotiations. A certain movie theater published "Bone-Corroding, Soul-Melting" in the film advertisements for the Wanhua Troupe. Who knew that this phrase caught the attention of the Chief of the Public Security Bureau, who specially sent a patrol officer to the theater to investigate, just how is it bone-corroding and soul-melting? Thus, due to the Chief's negotiations, the four words "Bone-Corroding, Soul-Melting" no longer met our eyes.

Welcoming the New and Sending off the Old is an Art

At the time when new officials take office and old officials step down, a group of local notables and gentry cannot avoid hosting banquets to welcome and send off, on the one hand, sending off the old officials with a farewell glance, and on the other hand, welcoming the new officials to show their enthusiastic welcome, so that they can have a way to advance in the future. This is a common practice everywhere, and Suzhou is even more a place where the upper and lower classes trust each other and the people's sentiments are harmonious. Therefore, in these days, when the County Magistrate and the Chief of the Public Security Bureau were changed at the same time, a group of social notables had to hold grand banquets to welcome the new and send off the old. The other day, at the welcoming and sending-off banquet in the Liu Garden, the editor-in-chief of a certain newspaper specially printed an article praising County Magistrate Zou Xiaogong's virtuous administration. The clean white paper had copperplate and eulogies, printed in a splendid manner, and the article also cited ancient and modern examples, combining classical and vernacular styles. However, it was flattering to an excessive degree, which inevitably caused contempt from the discerning. Thus, it aroused external reactions, and a few annotations were made to the article, turning a well-written and flattering article into a curse. The editor-in-chief shot himself in the foot and expressed extreme regret.

Seasonal Foods are Quickly Enjoyed

During and around the Dragon Boat Festival, there are many seasonal foods to eat, especially seasonal fruits. Green plums, yellow apricots and loquats, black lychees and waxberries, plus red Jinshan apples and russet American tangerines, are truly colorful and dazzling, and cannot help but arouse people's appetite. The local fruits of Suzhou, waxberries and loquats, are produced in large quantities, with those from Yaoshang in Guangfu and the Dongting West Mountain in Taihu Lake being the most famous. Among the dishes, although the shad is out of season, the fresh lotus leaves are already standing tall and transparent in the water. The steamed chicken with rice flour wrapped in lotus leaves is fresh, fatty, and fragrant, with a unique flavor. Xingla and soy sauce are also seasonal delicacies.

Finance: U.S. Purchase of Silver Inflates Currency Massively; Benchmark Gold Plummets Eight Dollars and Sixty Cents; Central Bank Injects Over a Thousand Bars, Still Difficult to Maintain 258

Yesterday, although there were no major changes in the overseas silver market, the gold market was weak due to unfavorable news, and sellers rushed in, making it difficult to maintain the ninety-dollar mark. The exchange market was loose and oversupplied, and the posted prices were raised, which also contributed to the decline. The Central Bank tried hard to buy spot gold at low prices, which was able to pull up the market, but the result was still difficult to maintain. In the morning, overseas silver market reports showed English silver contracted while American silver remained stable. The forward silver price on the London Metal Exchange rose by 0.5 to 1 cent, but the March silver price contracted by 1.2 cents. London raw gold rose by 1.5 pence, American cotton rose by 9 pounds, American wheat contracted by 0.5 points, and stocks rose by $1.54. Market sentiment was low, and pre-market trading fell to around $93. Reuters reported that the U.S. Treasury Department announced the total amount of silver purchased, which was paid for from the general fund and did not use the equalization fund. It also announced the amount of gold received according to the anti-hoarding order. This news had little impact. However, because dealers supplied U.S. dollars, the exchange market hardened, causing prices to fall immediately after opening. Then, due to advance knowledge that HSBC would post an increase of 12.5 points for English currency and 25 points for U.S. currency, market sentiment became even more depressed, and the ninety-dollar mark was broken. Banks were still bottom fishing, slightly fluctuating. Afterwards, the domestic market remained loose, and selling continued in the market. Bulls failed to rally and prices fell again. The Central Bank intervened to buy spot gold, which boosted market sentiment and was able to pull up the prices. Banks also took the opportunity to bottom fish and stabilize. The Seattle night market silver price was reported as rising 1.25 and falling 2.5 and unchanged. Market sentiment was not satisfied. Buyers were more enthusiastic and briefly broke through the ninety-dollar mark. However, market sentiment continued to be weak, and prices continued to fall. Lin Nian Summer silkworms discover silkworm plague. In the Linping area of Hangzhou, the hatching of summer silkworms went smoothly, and development was quite good. The early帮 already four眠, the late帮 three眠旺叶, but in the recent three days, the weather suddenly became strangely hot and stifling. Free Talk

The Current Stage and Future of the Mass Language Discussion 281

— Fu Donghua

Recently, the debate between Mr. Wang Maozu and Mr. Wu Yan'yin regarding classical Chinese and vernacular Chinese (specifically in Shanghai) has sparked two reactions: (1) concern over the revival of classical Chinese, leading to a felt need to strongly protest this trend; (2) a related feeling that the "vernacular" of the May Fourth Movement had inherent flaws (though this feeling didn't just arise now), and that there was a need for another, more wholesome literary language to replace it. This other language, to express its difference from the "vernacular" of the May Fourth Movement, and to facilitate future discussions about its construction, has been temporarily named "Mass Language" by some.

Up to now, participants in this discussion seem to pay little attention to point (1). In his article "The Future of Classical Chinese," Ling Mo says, "I assert that this protest is ineffective." Indeed, with Mr. Wang Maozu's repeated emphasis on "social need" constantly giving classical Chinese a shot in the arm, how effective can this protest be? Because Mr. Wang's protest against vernacular Chinese isn't just "idle groaning" either. He sees that many people learn English only to prepare to enter British "offices," so what purpose is there in learning Chinese besides preparing to enter Chinese "offices"? And now, Chinese "offices," whether government-run, business-run, or joint government-business ventures, only want classical Chinese, not vernacular Chinese, so Mr. Wang can't help but worry about young people. Yes, in today's China, life forces people to "speak human language to humans and ghost language to ghosts." (Here, "human language" and "ghost language" are used according to Mr. Liu Dabai's interpretation.) Typical popular figures, mostly picking up chalk, can write "white" "language" on the blackboard, and once they put down the chalk and wave the goose-feather fan that Mr. Ye Shengtao talks about, they can pick up a pen also made of feathers and write "as per the above" on red-lined paper – only such people

will rise to prominence. So Mr. Wang's concern about the decline of classical Chinese isn't without reason. But unfortunately, today's young people may not – and aren't allowed to – all plan to enter "offices" to rise to prominence, so Mr. Wang's good intentions may not be widely accepted, then Ling Mo's saying that "there's no need to worry about vernacular Chinese now" is absolutely true.

However, Ling Mo's response to the question he himself raised, "Is there something else to worry about after vernacular Chinese is utilized," with a simple "not necessarily" answer, seems a bit too careless. Because although words and words will naturally "separate," as Mr. Erye said (see "Trends" published on June 20, "The Separation of Words and Words"), if an accountant or lawyer doesn't clearly separate them, problems are bound to arise. So, bringing up the problem of "classical Chinese" and "vernacular Chinese" for discussion again can be considered "leftover articles from the May Fourth era" (also Mr. Erye's words). As for discussing how "vernacular Chinese" and "Mass Language" should be separated, it shouldn't be a "complete misfortune," right?

Until now, no one has objected to the term "Mass Language," but no one has emphasized its importance either, at most treating it as a synonym for "vernacular Chinese." For example, in Mr. Long Gonggong's article "A Step Further" (see "Trends" on June 25), there is a place where "Mass Language" and "Living Language" are bracketed under the three words "vernacular Chinese," as if these three terms are indistinguishable. In fact, the problem that Mr. Long wants to "take a step further" to discuss is the problem of "the separation of words and words" that Mr. Erye mentioned, so it seems necessary to give another language that has separated from "vernacular Chinese" a name first.

However, a name is often given different meanings by people, so Mr. Long's need for "a step further" is very natural and necessary. So far, the explanations given to "Mass Language" include the following:

(1) "Language that the masses can speak, understand, and see clearly." (Chen Zizhan)

(2) "Only proposing speaking, listening, and seeing as standards, I think, is not enough; writing must also be considered." (Chen Wangdao)

(3) "For the sake of respecting the interests of the masses, all writing should be a combination of spoken and written language." (Le Sibing)

(4) "Mass Language is not created by anyone, but something that progresses with the progress of the lives of the masses." (Shen Bao Reading Q&A)

(5) "Should be interpreted as a language representing the consciousness of the masses." (Hu Yuzhi)

However, because the two terms "masses" and "mass consciousness" are themselves too elastic, difficulties will still arise in discussions about practical construction. For example, the language that the urban masses can "speak and understand" may not be what the rural masses can "speak and understand"; also, can the hope of some backward rural masses for the appearance of a "True Son of Heaven" not be considered "mass consciousness"? Therefore, should Mass Language be allowed to occur and progress naturally, without any artificial "creation" and promotion? If our answer to the last question is affirmative, then all these discussions now are meaningless. Therefore, from the current stage of this problem discussion,

we can only grasp the following key points:

(1) "Masses" is a term opposed to all special individuals or special groups – from emperors to compradors – so the special language of all special individuals or special groups, whether oral or written, is not Mass Language. Classical Chinese, from the time it was used exclusively for writing, has been entirely the special language of special groups, so all classical Chinese is not Mass Language. "Vernacular Chinese," because it only takes "vernacular" as the standard and cannot defend itself from being utilized by special groups, "Vernacular Chinese" does not necessarily have to be Mass Language.

(2) "Mass Language" must learn from the masses on the one hand, and also be learned by the masses on the other, so its progress must at least have a little artificial help, just as the progress of history needs artificial help. For example, "lung disease," the most backward masses call it "wildcat fascination" (mythical), the next most backward masses call it "xu disease" (metaphysical), the standard Mass Language vocabulary should not allow the existence of these two terms, no matter how "vernacular" and how "living" they are. (As for novels describing the backward knowledge of the masses, of course, they are an exception.)

(3) For the reason of the second point above, it is currently impossible to "combine spoken and written language" (Mr. Hu Yuzhi has already said it), so the standard of "the masses must be able to understand" has to temporarily give way a little to the standard of "precise and accurate" advocated by Mr. Long (for example, in Beijing dialect, "automobile" is called "tram," and "gramophone" is called "talking box," both of which should be corrected in the Mass Language vocabulary). In other words, the scope of "masses" can only be narrowed temporarily. To be more specific, we can assume that the current level of education in higher primary schools is the standard for our Mass Language. As for the masses who are lower than this level and illiterate, of course, we still have to be more accommodating. Just as we sometimes don't use pronouns when talking to children, but language without pronouns cannot be regarded as standard language after all.

In the future, we hope that people can continue to "take a step further," "take another step further," and "take an even further step" to discuss this issue like Mr. Long Gonggong, gradually bringing up practical problems and solving them, and implementing them. Even if our protest is really ineffective, at least in the field of literature, we should first do a "clear the fields" work.

Finally, we must not forget that the people participating in this discussion now, in a certain sense, can also be regarded as a "special group," so whether our plan meets the needs of the real masses can only be judged by the real masses themselves.

Impressions of Zibo 282

— Luo Wang

(3) The Old Man Next to the Mine

"Rely on the mountain to eat the mountain, rely on the water to eat the water." People who rely on mines can only eat mines. But some eat very fat; some eat very bitter. When the Zichuan mine was first opened, there was a big man carrying a peanut basket selling peanuts in the mine area every day; later, as the number of miners gradually increased, the business gradually improved, from a basket to a stall; when the mine's coal implemented a contract sales system, he boldly contracted one coal, and in less than two years, he made tens of thousands of dollars.

This "big man rich man" is illiterate, but now his aura and conversation are such that no one can imagine his origins back then.

But he can still not forget the miners who helped him with their blood and sweat in the past, so he especially benefits the workers, helping those who have loans or illnesses. He also pities the miners who unfortunately died tragically without family members, and specially bought a large piece of charity land for burial. He is an "old man," and there are many workers in the "gang," so he became the chairman of the barren land chamber of commerce, the master of thousands of miners. The Shandong Provincial Government also erected a monument for him with the inscription "Benefits the People."

In addition, in Boshan, there are many more people who have made fortunes by transporting coal, from miners to rich people.

(4) The Sigh of the God-Carrying Team

When we visited the Dahuangdi coal mine, we first saw the Japanese people's houses and gardens, the cherry blossoms were in bloom, but the Japanese customs still existed.

There is a cemetery, planted with neat pines and cypresses, forming a wide cemetery path. Going up along the cemetery path, a conical sacrificial tower stands upright in the center, with the three characters "Memorial Tower" written on it, and under this tower is where the ashes of Japanese dead people are buried. There is a pavilion next to the tower, with a bell hanging inside, like an ancient temple. Another house, built with cement, was initially used to enshrine idols. It was established at the beginning of the revolutionary army's settlement of Shandong, the highest tide of the revolution! Therefore, a group of party department god-carriers took advantage of the dark night to smash those idols to pieces! Now the door has been sealed, and there is no god living in it!

But in other counties, superstition has recently revived. Based on hearsay, we have gained a little true news.

When the revolutionary momentum was very strong, the god-carrying team in a certain county in Shandong carried out their work very smoothly! Later, a group of pious men and women asked to automatically move the idols and seal them in a room outside the city, without destroying them. The god-carrying team agreed, so a group of superstitious men and women moved the gods back to the warehouse. When sealing the door, they muttered to themselves, roughly saying, "Dear bodhisattvas, please stay here temporarily. This is also a disaster. We will always avenge you in the future!"

Sure enough, in the 20th year of the Republic of China, a certain county suffered disasters repeatedly, and people said that it was caused by insulting the gods, so pious men and women jointly requested the authorities to return the gods to their positions! The authorities approved it, so they rebuilt the temple to welcome the gods, and the incense was revived, three or four times more prosperous than before, and the cost of superstition was no less than hundreds of thousands of dollars!

The revival of this Shintoism is a counter-evidence to the reversal of the times!

Upside Down Carrying 283

— Gong Han

Western philanthropists are afraid of seeing animal abuse. If they see chickens and ducks being carried upside down through the concession, they will take action. The so-called action, although it is nothing more than a fine, as long as you are willing to pay, you can still carry them upside down, but after all, action has been taken. So a few Chinese people protested loudly, thinking that Westerners treated animals preferentially and abused Chinese people, to the point that they were not as good as chickens and ducks.

This is actually a misunderstanding of Westerners. They despise us, that is true, but they don't put us below animals. Naturally, chickens and ducks, no matter what, will always be sent to the kitchen to be made into a big dish. Even if they are carried upright, it will not make up for their fate of ultimately returning to their roots. However, they cannot speak, cannot resist, so why add unnecessary abuse? Westerners talk about everything being beneficial. Our ancestors thought of the suffering of the people being "hung upside down," and they really described it appropriately, but they have not yet noticed the disaster of chickens and ducks being carried upside down. However, they had already attacked the boring cruelty of "slicing donkey meat alive" and "roasting goose paws alive" in their articles. This kind of thinking is something that both East and West have in common.

But people's minds seem to be a little different. People can organize, resist, be slaves, and be masters. If they are unwilling to work hard, they can certainly be forever reduced to stagehands. If they are free and liberated, they can achieve equality with each other. That fate is not necessarily to be sent to the kitchen and made into a big dish. The more inferior people are, the more they get the love of the master, so if a servant beats a comprador, the servant is reprimanded; if an ordinary person offends a servant, the ordinary person is blamed. There are no regulations in the concession prohibiting the abuse of Chinese people, precisely because we should have our own strength, our own skills, and be completely different from chickens and ducks.

However, we have heard the nonsense of benevolent people and righteous men from the classics, to solve the suffering of being hung upside down. Until now, we still can't help but always think of a little grace falling from the sky or some high place far away. Even more, we think that "it's better to be a dog in peaceful times than a human in times of chaos," it's okay to become a dog, but we are unwilling to unite and reform. Those who lament that they are not as good as the chickens and ducks in the concession have this kind of smell.

If there are too many of these kinds of people, everyone will be hung upside down, and even when they are sent to the kitchen, no one will save them temporarily. This is because we are ultimately human, but we are useless people.

Elopement (2) 284

— Written by Hungarian poet Petőfi Sándor, translated by Shi Yongyi

A few days later, the people in that small village where this incident occurred were talking about almost nothing but the elopement of Mrs. Andrew and her nephew Karl.

"It's right to deal with that old man like this! Why did he want to marry such a young and beautiful woman?"

"This is really difficult for me! I can't solve this problem. Perhaps it's because they love each other."

"Really – I guess."

"However, I feel very sorry for that old man. If he dies of sorrow because of this, I wouldn't be surprised at all."

"Poor man!"

"This unfortunate scandal –"

In those days, conversations like these were very common in this small village, while Karl and his beautiful and young aunt had already met in Pest. Their carriage was just about to arrive at the hotel entrance, while another carriage was driving away from there.

"Ah!" Mrs. Anna screamed in panic.

"I hope he loses his sight," Karl thought to himself, hurriedly looking in the direction of the carriage. The two of them then wrapped themselves up well in their coats. The person who saw them was a merchant from their hometown.

"He won't recognize us," Karl said reassuringly as they walked into their room at the hotel. "If he recognized us, he would definitely greet us."

"Thank God, he didn't recognize us!"

Does History Really Repeat Itself? 285

— Jia Wei

││ The Re-Enactment of the Debate Between "Classical Chinese" and "Vernacular Chinese" ││

From the "May Fourth Movement" to today, so much time has passed. And the debate between "classical Chinese" and "vernacular Chinese," at that time, had already determined the "victory or defeat." But today, there are actually people advocating "classical Chinese" again, and shouting the slogan of "Reviving Classical Chinese." In this way, some people say that this "old debt" will be re-examined.

True, the debate will certainly be re-enacted, but is this a repetition of history?

No, no, history will never repeat itself; however, due to the "stupidity" of mankind, they insist on repeating history!

Everyone must recognize that the decisive battle of the "May Fourth Movement" lay in the direct invasion of capitalism into China, which shook the very foundation of the inherent feudal system. At the same time, due to the needs of the objective conditions of society at that time, it was necessary to overthrow the dead language of "classical Chinese" and create the "recorded speech style." But at that time, only general intellectuals and the bourgeoisie under pure capitalism fought against the landed class and feudal remnants under the feudal system. Originally, no matter how the "victory or defeat" was decided at that time, due to the decision of objective historical conditions, with the increasing collapse of the feudal system, the "classical Chinese," which was the social consciousness pattern of its own, would inevitably decline with it.

However, due to the "stupidity" of mankind, today there are people who want to repeat history!

Indeed, today's feudal remnants are still powerfully and deeply lurking in all levels of society, so the sound of the "revival of classical Chinese" inevitably has a tendency to unfold with it.

Originally, the era is constantly moving forward, and social consciousness must also be constantly changing and evolving. However, if it is intentionally obstructed and oppressed by the strong force of mankind, the stagnation of social progress, and even the opening of a reverse gear, are all possible. Therefore, if we want society to progress and improve, we must strongly expose and attack this force. At the same time, we must first pay attention: writing and language are the hallmarks of every social consciousness, and they improve with the improvement of social consciousness. Therefore, in the need for our current stage of social consciousness, we must absolutely not repeat the history of the "May Fourth Movement," using the "foreign stereotype" vernacular of the general intellectual class and the bourgeoisie to fight against the dead "classical Chinese" of the current stage's "classical revival." We need to go a step further, with the evolution of social consciousness and the needs of the masses; we must build and advocate "Mass Language" to fight against the dead "classical Chinese," and at the same time, we must attack the "foreign stereotype" vernacular!

History never repeats itself, but due to the "stupidity" of mankind, they insist on repeating history. If we want society to improve and shorten its journey, we must attack and fight against all attempts to repeat history and engage in "reverse gear" behavior!

A Night Out in Early Summer 286

— Xuan Ling

It was an early summer evening, the night before the full moon. The moon, like a small ball, was not as bright and lovely as during the Mid-Autumn Festival, but there was not a single cloud in the sky, and she was nakedly exposed in the mysterious outer space. In the distance, a vast expanse of yellow paddy fields seemed to have no end. Isolated villages floated on the yellow paddy fields, and faint, sporadic lights shone from the forest. I and Zhen were boating in a small river on a night tour.

The oar broke the calm surface of the water, creating a layer of foam and making a tinkling sound. Then, at the starting point of the oar, there were swirls, and ripples rose on this side and that side, gradually expanding until they disappeared far away. A gentle breeze was blowing, and strands of willow green on the shore were dancing on the water. The water plants by the river trembled in the wind, making a rustling sound.

We rowed the boat to the wide surface of the river, and I stopped the oars, letting it drift in the water. Zhen compared this scene to a night tour on West Lake, but regrettably, there were no undulating mountain shadows reflected on the water. We bathed in the quiet moonlight, washing away the vulgar feelings in our hearts. I almost forgot that I was in the human world. Everything around was quiet, without any sound; occasionally, a few barks of dogs came from the distant farmhouses. I took out my harmonica from my pocket and began to play melodious tunes in the silent fields. Zhen also hummed something, harmonizing with my musical tunes. We really felt like we had entered a fairyland.

Two boats pulling boats came from the other end of the river, with red lights shining in the boats, and the voices of women and children could be heard from the cabin. The surface of the water, which was originally as flat as a mirror, reflecting the scenery on the shore, was immediately disturbed, and the moon in the water turned into several large and small ones connected in a line, and then slowly moved together and merged into one. The sound of the rocking oar could still be heard faintly, until it was vaguely unclear. The air gradually became quiet again, and Zhen also fell silent, savoring the poetic beauty. The night was deep, with a bit of coolness, and we quietly rowed back in the boat.

Snapshots of Life 287

— Jingbo

One summer evening, on my way home, the electric lights were already brightly lit. I passed several third-class small restaurants, places I had eaten at before, but I didn't feel like stepping inside at that moment. Was I hungry but didn't want to eat, or did I not feel hungry at all? Neither. I only had five copper coins and two dimes in my pocket. If I spent it all tonight, would I be drinking wind for lunch and dinner tomorrow? You might ask if I forgot to include breakfast snacks. Friend, you don't understand the economics of today's intellectuals. Breakfast snacks will have to wait until after the rejuvenation of the Chinese nation to be included in the budget.

Another small noodle shop receded behind me. Should I buy a bowl of plain noodles for twelve copper coins, or should I buy a cornbread bun for nine copper coins to take home? Before the dilemma was resolved, the distance between me and the noodle shop was already great. There's no need to go back for the noodles. I'll go forward to see if there are any cornbread buns. Too bad, I've already walked into the gentlemen's residential area. Even if a blind man sold cornbread buns, he wouldn't set up shop in these places. Let's move back toward home.

The plain noodle shop is right in front of me now. I'll exchange the two dimes for copper coins first, to avoid the noodle shop assistant saying the coins are bad. With a handful of copper coins, I called out, "Cook a bowl of plain noodles!" The portion was quite generous. The problem for tonight was resolved quite well. I'll buy a pack of cigarettes and go home to read.

The next morning, I looked at that reference book again. The issue I was researching hadn't yet formed a complete outline or concept. I'll take it slowly. I went outside. Several calm, elegant streets receded beneath my feet. The sun and I had more and more opportunities for trouble. I walked toward the bustling city, quickly resolving the lunch issue so I could go to the public reading room. It was getting late. Three small laborers had already occupied the first table, making a lively commotion. They were patrons of the noodle shop. The assistants were very insightful, knowing that if you didn't go to a restaurant for lunch and instead came to eat noodles, you must be penniless. Indeed, these three and I, although our clothes were different, generally couldn't escape the assistants' eyes. I ate and left, lit a cigarette, held it in my mouth, and strolled out. The leaves of the roadside trees cast some shadows, occasionally shielding me from the sunlight, which was at least a sign of sympathy for me. "Sugared Chestnuts! How much for a skewer?" I asked her. "Forty coppers." "Consider it." "Thirty coppers."

"No, thank you." Is it possible to not want it even at such a cheap price? It's not that I don't

Page 22

want it, but the thought of sometimes having to pay thirteen copper coins for a bowl of plain noodles fills my mind. If I spend three coins, I'll only have twelve left. What would happen if I encountered a special price on plain noodles? It's better not to buy them. The reading room is almost here.

I stepped inside. Oh, there are quite a few people. I casually looked at several newspapers. There was nothing of value. I went to the magazine rack and took down the "Rural Issues" that I hadn't finished reading last time. Both the quality and quantity presented fresh facts and reliable statistics. It couldn't be considered anything less than a relatively good essay. I browsed, read carefully... The time was already past four o'clock. I couldn't finish it immediately. I left, to be continued next time. People were almost all gone, leaving only me and two others. At this moment, this room revealed the greatness of its space again. As I was about to leave, I flipped through a newspaper that I hadn't had a chance to look at when I first arrived. I flipped to the page covering the table, and oh! It was covering a long strip of white paper! I reached out to pick it up. It was heavy—copper coins!

Abandoned property—I'll take it out and use it. I don't need to worry about anything else. I have to live, and I'm researching an unresolved issue! I'll have a glass of soda first, a large one, a large one! I opened the white paper and counted—forty-six copper coins. I could definitely get two bowls of plain noodles. Not picking up lost property is the way of a gentleman. But for someone like me, whose three meals aren't guaranteed, being a gentleman would mean going hungry. I'll have to bend the rules a little. When I become successful, then it won't be too late to advise others to be gentlemen and implement a new lifestyle movement.

The First Step in Dedicating Oneself to a Cause 288

— Hong Ben

Chinese people mostly have weak constitutions. "Fair-skinned scholars" have always been revered, a clear illustration of the nation's weakness! The existence and continuation of more than four thousand years of history seems to be entirely attributed to so-called scholars. Leaving aside the present, this was indeed the case in the past. Once a person became a scholar, their life became particularly noble. Because of the nobility of their lives, they would inevitably have special authority in society.

However, these so-called scholars are actually useless people. The most useless thing about them is the frailty and uselessness of their bodies. Because of their frailty, even if they possess "world-shaking ambitions," they are often buried in their studies and often collapse halfway. What use are they? May I ask, can a weak and thin horse "bear heavy burdens and travel far"?

How exactly were the scholars of ancient times so frail? From birth, they were confined to their rooms like daughters of wealthy families, instructed to bury themselves in their studies. As they grew older, "diligent study" was praised, and they were told to study by fireflies and to persevere with diligence. Those who grew up in wealthy families often took marrying a young wife as a way to urge their sons to study diligently. Fathers only hoped that their sons would work hard in their studies, and sons felt that this was the only way, the only lighthouse to a bright future.

Little did they know that the reality was far from it. As a result, nine out of ten scholars were disabled—nearsighted, hunchbacked, skinny! Tuberculosis was the representative image of scholars. This is how society forced them to be. So, what kind of impression does society have of them? It is said... "A thousand times noble, ten thousand times noble, a fair-skinned scholar!" Their faces were indeed snow-white, but their bodies were too wronged. Thus, generation after generation continued in this way, and the result was that each generation was worse than the last.

Now, many people are clamoring that the Chinese nation is too weak and too decadent. In this "age of strength," where arms bump and fists meet fists, we certainly cannot stand at the top, not even on equal footing. We can only submit below.

The time has come for us to have a sudden awakening! The elder Cai Yuanpei is, after all, "old in years but not in spirit." In an essay discussing the essential qualities of modern students, he sincerely instructed us that if we want to be a modern and promising student, the first thing we must have is a

strong physique like a son, in order to shoulder the mission of the times. The Western philosopher said, "A beautiful spirit resides in a beautiful physique." This is indeed a golden rule and worth making our a resounding slogan, worth making our life's motto. Young friends, student friends, we are born in this perilous era. If we want to have a future in our careers, we must grasp this point! Otherwise, no matter how "fair" your skin is, it will be useless today.

So, how can we have a strong physique? This requires a "health movement." Actively, it starts with suitable exercise. Passively, it starts with health preservation and hygiene. Various ball games, to the extent possible, we might as well play more often. Our lives must be regular, and we must preserve our health at all times.

Society and the nation have many things that are waiting for us to work hard on in the future. We are also people who have a desire for a career. At this moment, we must prepare, prepare our physiques.

Works by Ms. Huang Yingfen 289

— Huang Yingfen

Sister's Heart 290

— Wei

"Sister, stay here tonight, okay?" Ten-year-old Ju-zhen said, looking at her sister. Her sister seemed not to hear Ju-zhen's words and remained silent.

"Mom, is my sister staying here tonight?" Ju-zhen didn't get a response from her sister, so she turned to ask her mother.

"I don't know. Maybe she'll still go back after dinner," her mother replied faintly. At this time, the sky gradually darkened. The light blue sky gradually turned dark blue, then gradually darkened, finally becoming pitch black. The lights in Ju-zhen's house were turned on. After a while, dinner was served. So everyone gathered around the table to eat dinner. During dinner, the sister ate very quickly, as if she wanted to rush home after eating. Ju-zhen was very unhappy to see this. She thought that since her sister had gotten married, it had been difficult for her to spend a night at home. She was always very impatient and rushed home after eating dinner. Tonight, after dinner, she would definitely rush home again.

After dinner, everyone relaxed in the room. The sister and mother were talking. Ju-zhen looked at them and became impatient again.

"Sister, stay here," said Ju-zhen.

"I'm going back," the sister replied to Ju-zhen. Ju-zhen was very unhappy, only saying... "I knew it."

"Ju-zhen, your sister has to go back. She can stay here another day when she's free," her mother said to Ju-zhen very gently, as if she were comforting her.

The sister said goodbye to her mother and went back.

Ju-zhen listlessly walked into the room and lay down on her own bed. A question swirled in her little brain... Has sister's heart changed? Does she not love our home anymore?

A Sacrifice│Dedicated to the Spirit of a Newly Deceased Female Laborer│ 291

— Meng Han

No plain wine, no fresh flowers, no meager offering, I only have a heart, a handful of tears, a painful and sorrowful heart and the resonance of tears!

You, you unfortunate one! Your life was too pitiful, your fate too cruel. Before life, in illness, after death, concerning everything about you... if humanity still had some sympathy and pity, then no matter who it was, they would inevitably shed a tear of sadness for you!

You and I did not know each other, nor did we have any deep feelings; it was only because you came here to sell your sweat, and I was in a position superior to you, able to shed a few drops of sweat and blood less than you, and had the right to inquire about some of your affairs. Alas, I truly repent that I did not know your condition earlier. It wasn't until you had been bedridden for seven or eight days that your roommate reported it to me, and I immediately sent you to the hospital. Who would have thought that in less than two days, you would die with resentment?

I originally knew that life and death were so ordinary, and that people were only so related. Dying from illness is not a tragic event; the one who died was you – a laborer not worth a cent – not a remarkable person. What can't be dismissed with a sigh? But for the past few days, I have always felt as if something has pierced this heart, which has been wounded so many times. Every time I hear some fragmented stories about your life and the various tragic scenes after your death, it tightens the trembling of my heartstrings, and I can't help but shed tears!

I heard that... your family was poor, with aging parents... In order to make a living, you traveled far to Shanghai to enter a factory at a young age, and now they all depend on you for their livelihood. Alas, think of your parents, how can you bear to close your eyes?

I heard that... you were only eighteen years old this year. If you had been born as a noble lady, it would have been the golden age of youth. You could have scorned and disdained everything... But you had to swallow your anger, endure hardships, and bury yourself in the factory, working twelve hours a day. Heaven is merciless, not even allowing you to live such a miserable life for long. What else can be said?

I heard that... while you were sick, you slept alone, moaning alone. It wasn't until five or six days had passed that one of your cousins in Shanghai came to see you. At that time, your condition was already very serious, but your cousin heartlessly left without caring. In fact, she also had unavoidable difficulties... She was like you, exchanging a day's sweat for a day's living. She had no money to hire a doctor for you, and she had no way to maintain a few days of life and give up her work to take care of you, so she had to leave in the end. Poverty is so heartbreaking that even relatives cannot take care of each other!

I heard that... after you died, no one came, and nothing was prepared. Although a letter was sent to your family, your parents never came, perhaps because they had problems even with travel expenses? In the end, the factory took care of everything, and the cost was only a few tens of dollars. The meager coffin and clothing can be imagined. Before life and after death, it was like this, how can it not make people sad!

Ah! The world is narrow! Humanity is ruthless! You, me, us, a group of birds of the same fate! We will all be driven by the world and abandoned by humanity! Death is just the end of everything! Is it pain? Or maybe it's happiness?

You lonely and helpless soul! Come back!
